(عيني) ] كمن استأجر أرضا للزراعة على أن يردها مكروبة أو علق إجارتها لقدوم ،زيد وينبغي أن يستثني من عدم صحة التعليق ما لو قال للغاصب: فرغها وإلا فأجر كل شهر كذا، فلم يفرغ وجب المسمى رمز الحقائق: ٨٤/٢] (فتح) والإجازة : [ أي الرابع ] بالزاء المعجمة بأن باع فضولي عبده، فقال المولى أجزت البيع إذا جاء رأس الشهر، أو علق إجازته بشرط مثل أن يقول: إن قدم زيد، وكل ما لا تعليقه بالشرط لا يصح يصح تعليق إجازته، حتى لو زوج بنته البالغة بلا إذنها فبلغها الخبر ، فقالت: 'أجزت إن رضيت أمي بطلت الإجازة؛ إذ التعليق يبطل الإجازة اعتباراً بابتداء العقد. (عيني، فتح والرجعة [ أي الخامس: الرجعة بأن قال: إن رضيت ضرتك فقد رجعتك. (مسكين)] واعترض صاحب 'البحر' [٢٦٥/٦] على المصنف في ذكر الرجعة فيما يبطل بالشرط بناء على أنها تصح مع الإكراه والهزل واللعب والخطأ كالنكاح، فلو بطلت بالشرط الفاسد لما صحت مع الهزل. وأجاب في 'النهر' [٥٢٢/٣] بالتفرقة بينها وبين النكاح في أنه لا يشترط شهود للرجعة، ولا يجب بها عوض مالي، فتبطل بالشرط الفاسد بخلاف النكاح، وصورته بأن قال للمطلقة الرجعية راجعتك على أن تقرضني كذا، أو علقها بقدوم زيد؛ لأنها استدامة الملك، فتكون معتبرة بابتدائه، فكما لا يجوز تعليقها ابتداء فكذا لا يجوز تعليقها انتهاء أيضاً. [رمز الحقائق: ٨٤/٢] (فتح) والصلح عن مال [ أي السادس : الصلح إلخ؛ لأنه معاوضة مال بمال فيكون بيعا عيني)] وهذا فيما إذا كان عن مال بمال على خلاف الجنس بأن قال: صالحتك على أن تسكنني في الدار سنة، أو إن قدم زيد؛ لأنها معاوضة مال بمال فيكون بيعاً، فيبطل بالشرط، وإن كان على جنسه، فإن كان أقل المدعا كان حطاً وإبراء، وإن بمثله به كان قبضاً واستيفاء، وإن بأكثر منه كان رباً. (عيني، فتح) والإبراء عن الدين [ أي السابع ] الإبراء بأن قال: أبرأتك عن ديني على أن تخدمني شهراً أو إن قدم فلان؛ لأنه تمليك من وجه إسقاط من وجه، فوجب العمل بالشبهين بقدر الإمكان فقلنا: لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط إذا كان تعليقه بصريح الشرط عملا بشبه التمليك ويحتمل التقييد بالشرط عملا بشبهه الإسقاط، وذلك إذا لم يكن لمه حرف الشرط، فلو قال لمديونه: 'أدّ غدا نصفه على أنك بريء من الفضل ففعل برئ؛ لأنه لم يعلق البراءة - من
That which is nullified by a corrupt condition. The principle thereof is that every exchange of property for property is nullified by corrupt conditions, due to the hadith 'He forbade a sale with a condition'. And that which is an exchange of property for non-property, or is of voluntary gifts, is not nullified by corrupt conditions. Because corrupt conditions fall under riba; for riba is surplus without consideration, and the reality of corrupt conditions is an increase not required by the contract, so it contains surplus without consideration, which is riba. And that is not conceivable in non-financial exchanges like marriage and divorce for money and the like, nor in voluntary gifts, so the condition is nullified. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 4/542] And another principle: that suspension by a pure condition is not permissible in transfers of ownership. And when this is known, we say: Sale is an exchange of property for property, so it is corrupted by corrupt conditions due to what we have narrated. And it is permissible to suspend it absolutely if the condition is with the word 'in' (if), whether the condition is beneficial or harmful, except in one case: that he says 'I sold you this if so-and-so agrees', then it is permissible if he specifies a time of three days, because it is stipulating an option for a third party, and that is permissible. And if the condition is with the word 'ala' (on condition that), then if the condition is required by the contract, or compatible with it, or has an effect, or is customary such as delivery of the sold item or price, or term, or option, it does not corrupt, and the condition is permissible. And if it is not required by the contract, nor compatible, nor customary, then if there is benefit in the condition for the entitled parties, the sale is corrupted; otherwise not. (Fath)

Sale: i.e. the first: sale by selling a slave with the condition of his service for a month, so the sale is corrupt. (Ayni) Division: [i.e. the second: division between partners; because division has the meaning of exchange, so it becomes like sale, thus it is corrupted by a corrupt condition. (Ayni)] Such as if a deceased had a debt on people, and cash assets, so they divided the inheritance into debt and cash with the condition that the debt be for one of them and the cash for the others; this is corrupt. And a picture of its suspension with a condition: if they divide the house and stipulate the approval of so-and-so, this is also corrupt; because division has the meaning of exchange, so it becomes like sale, thus it is corrupted by a corrupt condition. Hire: [i.e. the third: hire by renting his house on condition that the lessee give him a loan or gift. (Ayni)] Like one who rents land for cultivation on condition that he return it plowed, or suspends its hire on the arrival of Zaid. And one should except from the invalidity of suspension the case where he says to the usurper: 'Vacate it, otherwise the rent each month is such-and-such', so he did not vacate, then the named rent is necessitated. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/84) (Fath) Ratification: [i.e. the fourth] with the letter 'z' (ijaza): such as if a fuduli sells a slave, and the owner says 'I ratified the sale when the month begins', or suspends his ratification on a condition like saying 'if Zaid comes'. And everything whose suspension by condition is not valid, its ratification is not valid; even if he marries his adult daughter without her permission, and the news reaches her, and she says 'I ratified if my mother approves', the ratification becomes void, because suspension voids the ratification by considering it like the commencement of the contract. (Ayni, Fath) Revocation: [i.e. the fifth: revocation by saying 'if your co-wife is pleased, then I have revoked you.' (Miskin)] The author of 'al-Bahr' [6/265] objected to the author (of Kanz) mentioning revocation among things nullified by condition, on the basis that it is valid under duress, jest, play, and mistake like marriage; so if it were voided by corrupt condition, it would not be valid under jest. And the author of 'al-Nahr' [3/522] answered by distinguishing between it and marriage: that witnesses are not required for revocation, and no financial compensation is due by it, so it is corrupted by a corrupt condition unlike marriage. Its picture: he says to a revocably divorced woman 'I have revoked you provided that you lend me such-and-such', or suspends it on the arrival of Zaid; because it is continuance of ownership, so it is considered like its commencement. Just as its suspension is not permissible initially, so also its suspension is not permissible finally. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/84] (Fath) Settlement (sulh) for property: [i.e. the sixth: settlement etc.; because it is exchange of property for property, so it is a sale (Ayni)] This is when it is property for property of a different genus: e.g., 'I settled with you on condition that you let me live in the house for a year', or 'if Zaid comes'; because it is exchange of property for property, so it is a sale, thus it is corrupted by the condition. And if it is of the same genus, then if less than claimed, it is reduction and release; if equal, it is receipt and collection; if more, it is riba. (Ayni, Fath) Release (ibra') from debt: [i.e. the seventh] ibra' by saying 'I release you from my debt on condition that you serve me for a month' or 'if so-and-so comes'; because it is a kind of transfer of ownership from one aspect and remission from another aspect, so it is necessary to act upon both aspects as much as possible. Thus we say: it does not bear suspension by a condition when it is suspended with an explicit condition, acting on the aspect of transfer, and it bears restriction by a condition acting on the aspect of remission. This is when there is no conditional word. So if he says to his debtor: 'Pay half of it tomorrow on condition that you are free from the excess', and he does, he is released; because he did not suspend the release - from
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage expounds the Hanafi ruling on corrupt conditions (shart fasad) in contracts. It begins with the maxim: any contract that is an exchange of property for property (mubadala mal bi mal) is corrupted by a corrupt condition, based on the hadith 'He forbade a sale with a condition'. Conversely, contracts that are exchange of property for non-property (like marriage or khul') or voluntary gifts (tabarru'at) are not corrupted by such conditions; rather only the condition is void. The reason is that a corrupt condition adds an extra benefit without countervalue, which is akin to riba. The passage then distinguishes between suspension (ta'liq) with 'in' (if) and stipulation (tashrit) with 'ala' (on condition). Suspension of a sale with 'in' is generally permissible except when it creates an option for a third party without time limit. Stipulation with 'ala' is evaluated: if the condition is normally part of the contract (like delivery, payment term, option), it is valid; if it benefits only one party and is unrelated, the sale becomes corrupt.

The passage then enumerates seven types of transactions that become void if a corrupt condition is attached:
1. Sale (bay'): e.g., selling a slave with condition of one month's service.
2. Division (qisma): e.g., dividing inheritance with condition that debt goes to one and assets to others.
3. Hire (ijara): e.g., renting land on condition that the tenant give a loan or gift, or suspending it on someone's arrival.
4. Ratification (ijaza): e.g., a fuduli's contract ratified with a condition or suspension; even a daughter's ratification of marriage with a condition becomes void.
5. Revocation (raj'a): e.g., suspending revocation on condition; this is a point of intra-Hanafi dispute: some argue revocation is like marriage (valid under jest), but the author maintains it is voided because no financial consideration is involved.
6. Settlement (sulh) for property: if it involves property of a different genus, it is like sale and voided by condition. If same genus, it may be reduction, receipt, or riba.
7. Release (ibra') from debt: it bears restriction (with 'ala') but not suspension (with 'in') because it is part transfer, part remission. The authority weight: this is from Fath (al-Qadir) and commentaries.

Key Terms
شَرْط فَاسِد (shart fasad): A condition that is extra to the contract and not required by it, providing a benefit to one party without countervalue, akin to riba.
مُبَادَلَة مَال بِمَال (mubadala mal bi mal): Exchange of property for property, i.e., a commutative contract.
تَعْلِيق (ta'liq): Suspension of a contract on a future condition using the word 'in' (if).
تَمْلِيك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of a sale where the seller stipulates that the buyer must give him a loan?
A) The sale is valid, but the condition is void.
B) The sale is corrupt (fasid).
C) The sale is void (batil).
D) The sale is valid and the condition is binding.

Key Takeaway
Contracts that exchange property for property are corrupted by conditions that add extra benefit without countervalue; only seven specific transactions are explicitly voided, and conditions natural to the contract remain valid.

Sale Invalidated by a Void Condition
Ruling on sale invalidated by a void condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a void condition in a sale contract that makes the contract fasid, and explain the distinction between fasid and batil in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A condition retaining usufruct for seller contradicts ownership transfer, making the sale fasid.

This lesson examines a classic example from the Hanafi texts: selling a slave with a condition that the seller may use the slave for a month after the sale. Such a condition is void because it conflicts with the essence of the sale, which is full transfer of ownership. According to the Hanafi school, the sale becomes fasid (voidable), not batil (void). Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper contract drafting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is a sale with an additional condition benefiting the seller. The ruling: the sale is fasid (voidable).
The text explicitly says 'the sale is void' i.e., fasid.
2
Locate the void condition
The condition is the seller's retention of the slave's service for one month after the sale. This is an extra benefit to the seller not part of the price.
Any condition that gives the seller a benefit beyond the price is suspect.
3
Understand why the condition is void
The condition contradicts the essence of sale: immediate and full transfer of ownership. The usufruct belongs to the buyer once ownership is transferred.
Hanafi principle: the sale contract must transfer both ownership and possession; retaining usufruct negates full transfer.
4
Distinguish fasid from batil
In Hanafi, fasid contracts have a defect but can be rectified by removing the condition; batil contracts are fundamentally invalid. Here, removing the condition restores validity.
Shafi'is would call such a contract batil because the condition renders the entire contract void.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Analogous: selling a car but condition that seller can use it for a week; the sale is fasid. The condition must be waived for the sale to become sahih.
If the condition is part of the price (e.g., seller financing), it is not void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البيع: أي الأول: البيع بأن باع عبداً وشرط استخدامه شهرا فالبيع فاسد.
The sale: i.e. the first: the sale such that he sells a slave and stipulates his service for a month, so the sale is void.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the section on miscellaneous matters. The author lists the sale as the first type of contract invalidated by a void condition. The example: selling a slave with the condition that the seller may use the slave for one month after the sale. Such a condition is void because it conflicts with the full transfer of ownership, which is the essence of the sale. Hence the sale itself becomes fasid (voidable). This is a basic Hanafi principle: any condition that provides a benefit to one party without being part of the consideration renders the contract defective.

Key Terms
بيع (bay'): A sale contract involving exchange of ownership for a price.
فاسد (fasid): A contract that is defective in its conditions but can be rectified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone sells a car but stipulates that he can use it for one day after the sale, what is the status of the contract according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The sale is sahih and the condition is valid.
B) The sale is fasid due to the void condition.
C) The contract is batil and cannot be rectified.
D) The condition is valid but the sale is revoked.

Key Takeaway
A sale becomes fasid when a void condition that benefits the seller is stipulated, but the contract can be corrected by removing that condition.

Division Void by Void Condition
Ruling on division invalidated by void condition with two examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on division (qisma) when accompanied by a void condition and explain why it is invalid.

Core Idea
A division with a void condition is like a sale with a void condition — both are invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling on the division of jointly owned property (qisma). The Hanafi school treats qisma as a form of exchange, akin to a sale. Consequently, any void condition attached to the division renders the entire transaction void (fasid). We will explore two examples from the text and understand the rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that qisma is the division of shared property, and the ruling is that it becomes fasid (void) if a void condition is attached.
2
Understand the legal analogy
The text explains that qisma contains the meaning of mubadala (exchange), so it is treated like a sale. Recall that a sale is invalidated by void conditions.
3
Apply the examples
Consider the two examples: (a) dividing estate where one takes debt and other asset with a condition; (b) dividing a house conditional on a third party's consent. Both are fasid.
4
Explain the rationale
The void condition spoils the contract because it introduces an element that contradicts the nature of the exchange. This is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh: any contract of exchange is invalidated by void conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقسمة: بأن كان للميت دين على الناس، والعين فاقتسموا التركة من الدين والعين وشرطوا أن يكون الدين لأحدهم والعين للباقين، فهذا فاسد، وصورة تعليقها بالشرط: بأن اقتسموا الدار، وشرطوا فيها رضاء فلان، فهذا فاسد أيضاً؛ لأن القسمة فيها معنى المبادلة، فصار كالبيع، فيفسد بالشرط الفاسد.
And the division: such that the deceased had a debt owed by people, and they divided the estate consisting of the debt and the asset, and they stipulated that the debt be for one of them and the asset for the rest, so this is void. And the form of suspending it by a condition: such that they divided the house and stipulated therein the consent of so-and-so, so this is also void; because division contains the meaning of exchange, so it becomes like a sale, thus it is invalidated by a void condition.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage presents the second ruling: qisma (division of jointly owned property) is invalidated by a void condition because it involves mutual exchange (mubadala). Two examples are given: (1) dividing the estate where one partner takes the debt and the other the physical asset with a condition; (2) dividing a house conditional on a third party's consent. Both are fasid because the division is akin to a sale, and a void condition spoils the contract. This emphasizes that any division with a condition that is not integral to the transaction renders it defective.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property among partners to ascertain individual shares.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is legally void and invalidates the contract if attached to an exchange contract.
مبادلة (mubadala): Exchange; mutual transfer of property or rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a division (qisma) invalidated by a void condition according to this text?
A) Because it is a form of gift.
B) Because it contains the meaning of exchange, like a sale.
C) Because it requires witnesses.
D) Because it is based on mutual consent.

Key Takeaway
A division (qisma) with a void condition is void (fasid) because it is like a sale; always ensure conditions in a division are valid.

Ratification Void by Void Condition
Ruling on ratification suspended by condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ratification suspended by a condition is void and identify examples of invalid conditional ratification.

Core Idea
Ratification cannot be suspended — a conditional ijaza is void.

This lesson addresses a key principle in Hanafi contract law: ratification (ijaza) must be unconditional. If the owner or a party attempts to suspend ratification by a future event or condition, the ratification is void. The text gives examples from sale and marriage to illustrate the rule, emphasizing that ta'liq (suspension) invalidates ijaza just as it invalidates the original contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is ijaza (ratification) of a contract made by an unauthorized agent (fuduli). The general ruling is that ijaza is valid only if unconditional.
2
Recognize when ratification becomes void
Ratification is void if it is suspended (mu'allaq) by a condition, such as a future time or event. The text provides examples: 'I ratify when the month begins' or 'if Zaid comes'.
The condition must be a future contingency; a past event does not suspend.
3
Apply the rule to the marriage example
If a woman's marriage is contracted without her permission, and she later says 'I ratify if my mother is pleased', the ratification is void. This shows that the rule applies across different contracts.
4
Understand the rationale via qiyas
The rationale is that ta'liq (suspension) is invalid for the original contract (initially), so it is also invalid for its ratification, since ratification retroactively confirms the contract.
This is a qiyas (analogy) from the beginning of the contract to its confirmation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإجازة: بأن باع فضولي عبده، فقال المولى أجزت البيع إذا جاء رأس الشهر، أو علق إجازته بشرط مثل أن يقول: إن قدم زيد، وكل ما لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط لا يصح تعليق إجازته، حتى لو زوج بنته البالغة بلا إذنها فبلغها الخبر، فقالت: "أجزت إن رضيت أمي" بطلت الإجازة؛ إذ التعليق يبطل الإجازة اعتباراً بابتداء العقد.
And the ratification: such that a person not authorized (fuduli) sells his slave, and the owner says, 'I ratify the sale when the beginning of the month comes,' or suspends his ratification by a condition such as saying, 'If Zaid comes,' and everything whose suspension by a condition is not valid, its ratification is not valid. Even if he marries his adult daughter without her permission, and the news reaches her, and she says, 'I ratify if my mother is pleased,' the ratification becomes void; because suspension invalidates ratification by analogy to the beginning of the contract.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage discusses ijaza (ratification) by the owner of a contract made by an unauthorized agent (fuduli). The ruling: ratification cannot be suspended (mu'allaq) by a conditional statement. Examples: saying 'I ratify when the month begins' or 'if Zaid comes' makes the ratification void. The same applies to a woman's ratification of her marriage: if she says 'I ratify if my mother is pleased,' it is void. The underlying principle is that suspension is not valid for acts that are based on immediate effect; since the original contract (if it were made by the owner) cannot be suspended, its ratification also cannot be suspended.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification of a contract made by an unauthorized agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a woman says, 'I ratify my marriage if my mother is pleased' according to this text?
A) The marriage is ratified upon her mother's pleasure.
B) The marriage is valid without ratification.
C) The ratification is void.
D) The marriage becomes dependent on the mother's consent.

Key Takeaway
A conditional ratification is void; ratification must be immediate and unconditional to be valid.

Settlement Void by Void Condition
Ruling on settlement for property invalidated by condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a settlement (sulh) involving property when the exchanged items are of different types or of the same type, and apply the ruling to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Settlement conditioned on future benefit is void because it is a sale; pure reduction is valid, equal exchange is valid, excess is riba.

In Hanafi fiqh, a settlement (sulh) involving property is not always straightforward. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the key distinction: if the settlement exchanges different types of property, it is treated as a sale and becomes invalid if a condition is attached. If the same type is exchanged, the ruling depends on whether the amount is less, equal, or more than the original claim. Understanding these categories helps ensure settlements are valid and avoid prohibited transactions like riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
The passage divides sulh involving property into two categories: when the exchanged property is of different types (e.g., money for usufruct) and when it is of the same type (e.g., money for money).
The type determination is crucial.
2
Analyze the different-type case
When types differ, the transaction is considered a sale (bay'). If a condition is attached (e.g., 'on condition you let me live in your house'), the contract becomes fasid (voidable) because the condition is void.
The condition does not necessarily invalidate the entire contract if removed; it makes it fasid.
3
Analyze the same-type case
When types are the same, the settlement is not a sale. Compare the settlement amount to the original claim: less => reduction (hatt) and release (ibra); equal => receipt (qabd) and settlement (istifa'); more => riba (usury) and invalid.
The excess is prohibited regardless of consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلح عن مال: وهذا فيما إذا كان عن مال بمال على خلاف الجنس بأن قال: صالحتك على أن تسكنني في الدار سنة، أو إن قدم زيد؛ لأنها معاوضة مال بمال فيكون بيعاً، فيبطل بالشرط، وإن كان على جنسه، فإن كان أقل المدعا كان حطاً وإبراء، وإن بمثله كان قبضاً واستيفاء، وإن بأكثر منه كان رباً.
And the settlement for property: this is when it is property for property of a different type, such as his saying, 'I settle with you on condition that you let me live in the house for a year,' or 'if Zaid comes.' Because it is an exchange of property for property, so it becomes a sale, thus it is invalidated by a condition. And if it is of the same type, then if it is less than the claimed amount, it is reduction and release; if equal, it is receipt and settlement; if more, it is riba.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage discusses sulh (settlement) involving property. When sulh involves an exchange of property of different types (e.g., money for usufruct), it is treated as a sale, so a void condition makes it fasid. Examples: settling a debt by agreeing to live in the debtor's house for a year, or conditional on someone's arrival. However, if the exchanged property is of the same type (both are money), different rules apply: if the settlement amount is less than the claim, it is a reduction (hatt) and release (ibra); if equal, it is a receipt; if more, it is riba (usury) and prohibited.

Key Terms
صلح عن مال (sulh 'an mal): A settlement agreement where one party gives property to settle a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says, 'I settle with you on condition that you let me live in your house for a year,' what is the ruling according to the text?
A) The settlement is valid because it is a form of gift.
B) The settlement is void because it is like a sale with a condition.
C) The settlement is valid because it is a reduction.
D) The settlement is void because it is riba.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a property settlement in Hanafi fiqh hinges on whether the exchanged items are of the same type; if different, it is a sale voidable by conditions; if same, it is valid only if not in excess of the claim.

Validity of Ibra' with Conditions: Suspension vs Restriction
Ruling on release from debt with condition or suspension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid conditions in 'ibra' (release from debt) and apply the ruling to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Ibra' is partly transfer, partly waiver — explicit condition words invalidate, but restrictions without condition words are valid.

This passage addresses a critical nuance in Hanafi contract law: can you attach a condition to forgiving a debt? The answer depends on whether the wording suspends the release (invalid) or merely restricts it (valid). We'll unpack the dual nature of ibra' and see how the Hanafi jurists balance both aspects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
Recognize that the passage deals with ibra' (release from debt), a unilateral act of forgiveness.
Ibra' can be spoken by the creditor to the debtor.
2
Classify the wording
Distinguish between ta'liq (suspension using explicit condition words like 'if', 'when') and taqyid (restriction without those words).
Explicit condition words in Arabic: 'in', 'idha', 'mata'.
3
Understand the dual nature
Ibra' combines tamlik (transfer of right) and isqat (waiver of claim). Tamlik cannot be suspended; isqat can be restricted.
This duality forces a balanced ruling.
4
Apply the principle
If suspension (ta'liq) → invalid; if restriction (taqyid) → valid.
The passage gives examples: 'on condition that you serve' is valid, 'if you pay' is invalid.
5
Verify with examples
Check the creditor's exact words. 'Pay half tomorrow on condition that you are free from the remainder' is valid; 'if' or 'when you pay' is not.
This step ensures practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإبراء عن الدين: بأن قال: أبرأتك عن ديني على أن تخدمني شهراً أو إن قدم فلان؛ لأنه تمليك من وجه وإسقاط من وجه، فوجب العمل بالشبهين بقدر الإمكان فقلنا: لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط إذا كان تعليقه بصريح الشرط عملا بشبه التمليك ويحتمل التقييد بالشرط عملا بشبه الإسقاط، وذلك إذا لم يكن حرف الشرط، فلو قال لمديونه: "أد غدا نصفه على أنك بريء من الفضل" ففعل برئ؛ لأنه لم يعلق البراءة بصريح الشرط بل أتى بالتقييد، ولو قال: "إن" أو "إذا" أو "متى أديت" لا يصح؛ لأنه أتى بصريح الشرط وهي لا تحتمل التعليق بالشرط.
And the release from debt: such that he says, 'I release you from my debt on condition that you serve me for a month' or 'if so-and-so arrives.' Because it is from one aspect a transfer (tamlik) and from another aspect a waiver (isqat), so it is necessary to act according to both aspects as much as possible. Thus we say: it does not tolerate suspension by a condition when it is suspended by an explicit condition, acting according to the aspect of transfer; and it tolerates restriction by a condition, acting according to the aspect of waiver, and that is when the word of condition is not present. So if he says to his debtor, 'Pay half tomorrow on condition that you are free from the remainder,' and he does so, he becomes free; because he did not suspend the release with an explicit condition but used restriction. And if he says, 'if' or 'when' or 'whenever you pay,' it is not valid; because he used an explicit condition, and it does not tolerate suspension by condition.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage explains the rules for ibra' (release from debt) with conditions. Ibra' has a dual nature: it is like a transfer (tamlik) in that it involves giving up a right, and like a waiver (isqat) in that it removes a liability. Due to this dual nature, the ruling balances both: if the condition is expressed explicitly with words like 'if' (in, idha, mata), the ibra' is invalid because it resembles tamlik which cannot be suspended. However, if the condition is merely a restriction without the explicit conditioning word (e.g., 'pay half tomorrow on condition that you are free'), it is valid because it resembles isqat which can be restricted. The key distinction is the presence of explicit condition words.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Release from a debt, forgiving what is owed.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bi al-shart): Suspending a legal act upon the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following statements would result in a valid release from debt?
A) 'I release you if you pay half tomorrow.'
B) 'Pay half tomorrow on condition that you are free from the remainder.'
C) 'I release you when Zaid comes.'
D) 'I release you on condition that you serve me for a month.'

Key Takeaway
Ibra' with a condition is valid only if the condition word is absent; explicit 'if/when' invalidates the release.

Contracts That Remain Valid Despite a Corrupt Condition
Lists contracts that remain valid despite a corrupt condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that non-financial-exchange contracts are not invalidated by corrupt conditions and apply it to the ten contracts listed.

Core Idea
Non-exchange contracts stay valid; only the corrupt condition is void.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle from Kanz al-Daqaiq: contracts that are not financial exchanges (mu'awadah maliyyah) are not invalidated by a corrupt condition (shart fasid). The passage lists ten specific contracts and provides examples, explaining that the condition is void but the contract remains sahih. We will walk through each contract and understand the underlying reasoning, building on the general rule that conditions are specific to riba and exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contracts
List the ten contracts mentioned in the passage: loan, gift, charity, marriage, divorce, khul', emancipation, pledge, bequest of guardianship, and will.
These are the first ten of twenty-seven contracts according to the author.
2
Understand the General Principle
The passage states that conditions invalidate only financial exchange contracts. Since these contracts are not financial exchanges, a corrupt condition does not affect the contract itself; it only voids the condition.
The principle is linked to the prohibition of riba and gharar in exchange.
3
Apply to Each Contract
For each contract, the text gives a typical example of a corrupt condition and confirms that the contract remains valid. Analyze each example to see how the condition is void while the contract stands.
Focus on the ruling for each: loan (condition of benefit to lender), gift (condition of compensation), charity (condition of return), marriage (condition of maintenance/dower), etc.
4
Note the Exception in Gift
The passage mentions a nuance: in gift (hibah), if a condition of compensation (iwad) is stipulated and the compensation is valid property, the condition is considered and the gift becomes a sale-like exchange. Otherwise, the condition is void.
This is the chosen view (al-mukhtar) in the Hanafi school.
5
Synthesize the Rule
Conclude that the common thread is the absence of monetary exchange. These contracts are either benevolent (loan, gift, charity), personal status (marriage, divorce, khul'), or security/commitment (pledge, bequest, emancipation, will).
The rule safeguards the validity of the contract's primary purpose.

(عيني)] كما إذا تصدق على رجل بدراهم على أن يرد عليه شيئاً منها، فالصدقة جائز والشرط باطل. (فتح) والنكاح [ أي الرابع النكاح (عيني)] بأن تزوج امرأة على أن ينفق عليها في كل شهر مائة دينار، فالنكاح جائز ونفقة مثلها، وكذا لو قال: تزوجتك على أن لا يكون لك مهر ، يصح النكاح ويفسد الشرط، ويجب عليه مهر المثل كما عرف في موضعه والطلاق بأن طلق على أن لا تتزوجي بآخر بعد العدة وقبلت المرأة، طلقت، تزوجت أو لا، وبطل الشرط، وقوله: "والخلع" بأن اختلعت من زوجها بشرط أن لا يكون الولد الصغير لها، صح الخلع دون الشرط. (عيني، فتح والخلع أي السادس خلع بأن قال خالعتك على ألف بشرط أن يكون لي الخيار مدة كذا. Book of Sales, Chapter of Miscellaneous Matters: and what is not invalidated by a corrupt condition: Loan, Gift, Charity, Marriage, Divorce, Khul', Emancipation, Pledge, Bequest of Guardianship, and Will. [i.e. the corrupt condition has no effect on it, rather the condition is void and the contract is valid, and these are twenty-seven contracts. (Ayni, Fath)] i.e. the contracts that are not invalidated by corrupt conditions are twenty-seven according to what the Shaykh mentioned; because of what preceded that conditions are the chapter of riba, and that it is specific to financial exchange, and these contracts are not financial exchange, so corrupt conditions do not affect them; rather the conditions are void and the contracts are valid. For example, in loan if he said: I lend on condition that you write to your friend such-and-such until he repays the debt, the condition is void and the loan is valid. And likewise in all these contracts. Attaching a loan is haram and the condition is not binding, and it is construed as when he attaches it to a condition containing benefit for the lender, due to the prohibition against a loan that draws benefit. (Ayni, Fath) Loan: the first: loan that he said: I lend to you on condition that you serve me for a month, then the condition is void. (Ayni) And gift: [i.e. the second: gift that he gave a slave girl on condition that her pregnancy be for the donor. (Ayni)] And in al-Khulasa: the chosen view is that the condition of compensation in gift is considered. And this is assumed regarding something that can be compensation, like cash and commodities. If a woman gifts her dower to her husband on condition that he not divorce her, and the husband accepts, the gift is valid whether he divorces her or not, because not divorcing is not valid as compensation, so its condition is not considered. And charity: [i.e. the third: charity that he gives charity to a man on condition that he serve him for a week, for example. (Ayni)] Like when he gives charity to a man with dirhams on condition that he return something of them to him, the charity is valid and the condition is void. (Fath) And marriage: [i.e. the fourth: marriage (Ayni)] that he married a woman on condition that he spend on her one hundred dinars every month, the marriage is valid and she gets the maintenance amount similar to her. And likewise if he said: I married you on condition that you have no dower, the marriage is valid and the condition is corrupted, and he owes dower similar to her as known in its place. And divorce: that he divorced on condition that she not marry another after the idda, and the woman accepted, she is divorced whether she marries or not, and the condition is void. And his statement: "and khul'" that she divorced from her husband on condition that the young child not be hers, the khul' is valid without the condition. (Ayni, Fath) And khul': the sixth: khul' that he said: I divorce you for one thousand on condition that I have the option for such a period. (Ayni) And emancipation: the seventh: emancipation that he said: I free you on condition that the wala' between us is not [valid] [...] and pledge: the eighth: pledge that he pledged my slave to you on condition that he serve me. (Ayni) And bequest of guardianship: [i.e. the ninth: bequest of guardianship that he said: I bequeath to you on condition that you marry my daughter (Ayni)] It cannot be said: the will is ownership while its attachment to a condition is valid; because we say: it is not ownership immediately but a commitment of donation. Ownership is only eventual after death, and consideration is for the present. So it is from the commitments by which one swears, so its attachment to a condition is permissible. And the will: [i.e. the tenth: the will that he said: I will to you one third of my property if so-and-so approves. (Ayni)] i.e. he said: the will regarding property, because its wording indicates ownership after death; it cannot be conceived as present except metaphorically. (Ayni, Zayla'i)
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage lists contracts that are NOT invalidated by a corrupt condition (shart fasid). The general principle is that conditions invalidate only financial exchange contracts (mu'awadah maliyyah). These ten contracts (of the twenty-seven mentioned) are not financial exchanges, so a corrupt condition does not affect them; the condition is void but the contract remains valid. The contracts enumerated are: (1) Loan (qard): if a condition imposes benefit on the lender, the condition is void but the loan stands. (2) Gift (hibah): a condition for compensation may be considered if the compensation is valid; otherwise the gift stands without the condition. (3) Charity (sadaqah): conditions like service are void, charity valid. (4) Marriage (nikah): conditions regarding maintenance or dower are void; marriage valid with proper dower. (5) Divorce (talaq): conditional divorce is effective; condition void. (6) Khul': conditions about children are void; khul' valid. (7) Emancipation ('itq): condition on wala' is void. (8) Pledge (rahn): condition about service is void. (9) Bequest of guardianship (isa'): can be conditional because it is a commitment, not immediate ownership. (10) Will (wasiyyah): can be attached to condition because it is ownership after death, not immediate. The text emphasizes that these are not financial exchanges, so corrupt conditions do not affect them.

Key Terms
القرض (al-qarḍ): A loan of property to be repaid later; not a financial exchange because it is a benevolent contract.
الهبة (al-hibah): A gift; a donation without immediate exchange, so conditions do not invalidate it.
النكاح (al-nikāḥ): Marriage contract; not a financial exchange, so conditions on dower or maintenance do not invalidate it.
الشرط الفاسد (al-sharṭ al-fāsid): A condition that is legally invalid (corrupt) because it contradicts the purpose of the contract or is prohibited.
المعاوضة المالية (al-muʿāwaḍah al-māliyyah): A financial exchange contract where both parties give and receive something of value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The loan is invalid and the condition is void.
B) The loan is valid and the condition is binding.
C) The loan is valid and the condition is void.
D) The loan is invalid and the condition is binding.

Key Takeaway
Non-financial-exchange contracts such as loan, gift, marriage, and others remain valid despite a corrupt condition; only the condition is void.

8 min
Contracts Not Invalidated by an Invalid Condition
Listing contracts where invalid condition is void but contract valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between financial exchange contracts (mu'awada maliyya) and non-exchange contracts, and state the effect of an invalid condition on each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In non-exchange contracts, an invalid condition is void but the contract remains valid.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq enumerates a wide range of contracts that are not invalidated by an attached invalid condition (shart fasid). The Hanafi school builds on the principle that conditions are relevant only to financial exchanges, as they fall under the prohibitions of riba. Non-exchange contracts—such as loans, gifts, marriage, divorce, and many others—remain valid even if a void condition is included; only the condition is null. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying fiqh rulings in daily transactions.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the overarching principle
The text states: 'Conditions are the chapter of riba and are specific to financial exchange.' Recognize that only mu'awada maliyya (e.g., sale, lease) are susceptible to invalidation by an invalid condition. All other contracts are unaffected in their validity.
2
Work through the listed contracts
The passage names twenty contracts (loan, gift, charity, marriage, divorce, khul', emancipation, pawn, appointment, will, partnership, mudaraba, judgeship, governorship, suretyship, transfer of debt, agency, rescission, kitaba, permission for slave). For each, note that the contract is sahih (valid) and only the condition is batil (void).
3
Identify the exception: kitaba
Kitaba (contract of manumission) has a dual nature: it resembles sale (property aspect) and marriage (personal aspect). If the invalid condition is intrinsic (e.g., countervalue is wine), the contract is invalidated; if extrinsic (e.g., a restriction on movement), the condition is void and the contract stands.
This shows that the rule is not absolute; contracts with a financial exchange element may be affected.
4
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Take a hypothetical: a man lends money on condition that the borrower provides a service. Since a loan is not a financial exchange, the condition is void and the loan is valid. Similarly, a gift conditioned on the recipient performing an act is valid; only the condition is void.
Always check whether the contract is a financial exchange to determine the outcome.

أي العقد الذي بالشرط الفاسد [أي لا تؤثر فيه الشرط الفاسد بل يبطل الشرط ويصح العقد، وهذه سبعة وعشرون عقدًا. (عيني، فتح)] أي العقود التي لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة سبعة وعشرون على ما ذكره الشيخ؛ لما سبق من أن الشروط باب الربا، وأنه يختص بالمبادلة المالية، وهذه العقود ليست بمعاوضة مالية، فلا تؤثر فيها الشروط الفاسدة بل تبطل الشروط وتصح العقود، مثلاً في القرض لو قال: أقرض على أن تكتب إلى صديقك بكذا وكذا حتى يوفي الدين، يبطل الشرط ويصح القرض، وهكذا في العقود كلها، وتعليق القرض حرام والشرط لا يلزم، وهو محمول على ما لو علقه بشرط فيه منفعة للمقرض؛ لنهيه عليه عن قرض جر نفعًا. (عيني، فتح) القرض: الأول: القرض بأن قال: أقرضتك بشرط أن تخدمني شهرًا، فإنه يبطل الشرط. (عيني)
والهبة [أي الثاني الهبة بأن وهب جارية بشرط أن يكون حملها للواهب. (عيني)] وفي "الخلاصة": المختار أن شرط العوض في الهبة معتبر، وهذا مفروض فيما يصلح عوضًا كالنقود والعروض، فلو وهبت امرأة مهرها من زوجها على أن لا يطلقها وقبل الزوج، صحت الهبة طلقها أو لا؛ لأن عدم الطلاق لا يصلح عوضًا، فلا يكون شرطه معتبرًا. والصدقة [أي الثالث: الصدقة بأن تصدق على رجل على أن يخدمه جمعة مثلاً. (عيني)] كما إذا تصدق على رجل بدراهم على أن يرد عليه شيئًا منها، فالصدقة جائز والشرط باطل. (فتح) والنكاح [أي الرابع النكاح (عيني)] بأن تزوج امرأة على أن ينفق عليها في كل شهر مائة دينار، فالنكاح جائز ونفقة مثلها، وكذا لو قال: تزوجتك على أن لا يكون لك مهر، يصح النكاح ويفسد الشرط، ويجب عليه مهر المثل كما عرف في موضعه والطلاق بأن طلق على أن لا تتزوجي بآخر بعد العدة وقبلت المرأة، طلقت، تزوجت أو لا، وبطل الشرط، وقوله: "والخلع" بأن اختلعت من زوجها بشرط أن لا يكون الولد الصغير لها، صح الخلع دون الشرط. (عيني، فتح) والخلع أي السادس خلع بأن قال خالعتك على ألف بشرط أن يكون لي الخيار مدة كذا. (عيني) والعتق أي السابع العتق بأن قال: أعتقك أن لا يكون الولاء بيننا مسكين والرهن: أي الثامن: الرهن بأن رهنت عندك عبدي بشرط أن يخدمني. (عيني) والإيصاء [أي التاسع الإيصاء بأن قال: أوصيت إليك على شرط أن تتزوج ابنتي (عيني)] لا يقال: الوصية تمليك مع أنه يصح تعليقها بالشرط؛ لأنا نقول: ليست تمليكًا حالاً بل التزام التبرع، وإنما التمليك مآلاً بعد الموت والعبرة للحال، فهي من الالتزامات التي يحلف بها، فيجوز تعليقها بالشرط. والوصية [أي العاشرة: الوصية بأن قال أوصيت لك بثلث مالي إن أجاز فلان. (عيني)] أي قال: الوصية بالمال؛ لأن لفظها ينبئ عن التمليك بعد الموت؛ إذ لا يتصور أن يكون للحال إلا مجازًا. (عيني، زيلعي)
والشركة [أي الحادي عشر: الشركة بأن قال شاركتك على أن تهديني كذا (عيني) بأن تفاوت المال في شركة العنان وغيرها، وشرط الربح والوضيعة نصفين، قالوا: الوضيعة فاسدة، يعني كونها نصفين فاسد؛ لأنها تتبع رأس المال في التفاوت والمضاربة [أي الثاني عشر: المضاربة. (مسكين) بأن شرط الوضيعة على المضارب صحت المضاربة وبطل الشرط، وتكون الوضيعة على رب المال ولو شرط من الربح عشرة دراهم، فسدت لا من حيث أنها تبطل بالشرط الفاسد؛ إذ هي لا تبطل به بل لقطع الشركة. (فتح) والقضاء: [أي الثالث عشر: القضاء] كما إذا ولاه الخليفة بلدة كذا على أن لا يعزل أبدًا، أو ولاه مؤبدًا، فالشرط باطل، وكان له عزله ولو بلا جناح والإمارة [أي الرابع عشر: الإمارة بأن قال الخليفة: (عيني)] وليتك على أن لا تركب، وقال في "البزازية": ولو شرط عليه أن لا يرتشي، أو أن لا يشرب الخمر، صح التقليد والشرط، وإن فعل شيئًا من ذلك لعزل والقضاء والإمارة تولية وتفويض محض، فجاز إضافتهما وتعليقهما بالشرط. (زيلعي، فتح) والكفالة: [أي الخامس عشر: الكفالة وهي من باب الالتزامات، فيجوز إضافتها إلى الزمان، وتعليقها بالشرط الملائم، ولو كان الشرط غير ملائم، يفسد الشرط، وتصح الكفالة بأن قال: كفلت عن غريمك على أن تقرضني كذا. والحوالة: [أي السادس عشر: الحوالة بأن قال: أحلتك على فلان بشرط أن لا ترجع على عهده التوى. (عيني)] وهي من الالتزامات التي لا يحلف بها، فلا يصح تعليقه، إلا أنه يستلزم الدين عليه. (عيني، زيلعي) والوكالة: [أي السابع عشر: الوكالة (عيني) وهي من باب الإطلاقات ومن جملة الإسقاطات، فلو قال: وكلتك على أن تبرئني مما لك علي، يصير وكيلاً ويبطل الشرط. والإقالة : [أي الثامن عشر: الإقالة. (مسكين)] بأن اشترى رجل من آخر عبدًا بألف درهم وتقابضا، ثم قال البائع أقلني حتى أؤخر لك الثمن سنة، فقال: أقلت، جازت الإقالة دون التأخير. (زيلعي، فتح) والكتابة [أي التاسعة عشرة: الكتابة بأن كاتب بشرط أن لا يخرج من الكوفة إلا بإذنه، أو على أن لا يعامل فلانًا، أو على أن يعمل في نوع من التجارة، فإن الكتابة على هذا الشرط تصح ويبطل الشرط، فله أن يخرج من البلد، ويعمل ما شاء من أنواع التجارة مع أي شخص شاء، وذلك لأن هذا الشرط غير داخل في صلب العقد، وأما إذا كان داخلًا في صلب العقد بأن كان في نفس البدل كالكتابة على خمر ونحوها، فإنها تفسد به؛ لأن للكتابة شبهًا بالبيع من حيث أن العبد مال في حق المولى، وشبهًا بالنكاح من حيث أنه ليس بمال في حق نفسه، فعملنا بالشبهين فشبهها بالبيع يفسد إذا كان المفسد في صلب العقد، ولشبهها بالنكاح لا تبطل بالشرط الزائد. [رمز الحقائق: ٨٦/٢] وإذن العبد إلخ [أي العشرون: إذن العبد بأن قال لأهل السوق: أذنت لهذا العبد في التجارة بشرط أن يعلمني صح إذنه وبطل الشرط، ولو قال لعبده أذنت لك أن تتجر إلى شهر، .
The book of sales. Chapter of miscellaneous matters. And what is not invalidated by an invalid condition: loan, gift, charity, marriage, divorce, khul', emancipation, pawn, appointment (isa'), and will (wasiyyah). That is, the contract that [is not affected] by the invalid condition, i.e., the invalid condition does not affect it; rather the condition becomes void and the contract is valid. And these are twenty-seven contracts. (Ayni, Fath) That is, the contracts that are not invalidated by invalid conditions are twenty-seven according to what the Shaykh mentioned; because of what preceded: that conditions are the chapter of riba, and it is specific to financial exchange, and these contracts are not financial exchange, so invalid conditions do not affect them; rather the conditions are void and the contracts are valid. For example, in a loan if he said: I lend to you on condition that you write to your friend such-and-such until he pays the debt, the condition is void and the loan is valid. And likewise in all contracts. And suspending a loan is prohibited and the condition does not bind. And it is interpreted as when he suspends it on a condition containing benefit for the lender, because of his ﷺ prohibition of a loan that draws benefit. (Ayni, Fath) The loan: first: the loan when he says: I lend to you on condition that you serve me for a month, then the condition is void. (Ayni) And gift: second: gift when he gives a slave-girl as a gift on condition that her pregnancy belongs to the donor. (Ayni) And in al-Khulasa: the chosen view is that the condition of compensation in a gift is considered. And this is assumed regarding what is suitable as compensation, like money and goods. So if a woman gifts her dower to her husband on condition that he does not divorce her, and the husband accepts, the gift is valid whether he divorces her or not, because the absence of divorce is not suitable as compensation, so its condition is not considered. And charity: third: charity when he gives charity to a man on condition that he serves him for a week, for example. (Ayni) As if he gives charity to a man of dirhams on condition that he returns something from it to him, the charity is valid and the condition is void. (Fath) And marriage: fourth: marriage (Ayni) such as when a man marries a woman on condition that he spends on her one hundred dinars every month, the marriage is valid and she gets the maintenance of her like. Likewise if he said: I married you on condition that you have no dower, the marriage is valid, the condition is corrupted, and he must pay the dower of the like as known in its place. And divorce: when he divorces on condition that she does not marry another after the 'idda, and the woman accepts, she is divorced whether she marries or not, and the condition is void. And his saying: 'and khul'': when she divorces herself from her husband on condition that the young child is not for her, the khul' is valid but not the condition. (Ayni, Fath) And khul': sixth: khul' when he says: I divorce you for one thousand on condition that I have the option for such a period. (Ayni) And emancipation: seventh: emancipation when he says: I free you on condition that the wala' is not between us. (Miskin) And pawn: eighth: pawn when I pawn my slave with you on condition that he serves me. (Ayni) And appointment (isa'): ninth: appointment when he says: I appoint you as executor on condition that you marry my daughter. (Ayni) It is not said: the will (wasiyyah) is a transfer of ownership even though suspending it on a condition is valid; because we say: it is not a transfer of ownership at present but rather a pledge of gratuitous transfer (tabarru'), and ownership only arises eventually after death, and consideration is for the present; so it is among commitments (iltizamat) which one takes an oath on, so it is permissible to suspend it on a condition. And the will (wasiyyah): tenth: the will when he says: I bequeath to you a third of my property if so-and-so permits. (Ayni) That is, he said: the will regarding property, because its wording indicates transfer of ownership after death, as it cannot be imagined for the present except metaphorically. (Ayni, Zaylai) And partnership: eleventh: partnership when he says: I partnered with you on condition that you give me such-and-such as a gift. (Ayni) Such as disparity of capital in a partnership of 'inan and others, and stipulation of profit and loss equally. They said: the loss clause is invalid, meaning that it being equal is invalid, because it follows capital in disparity. And mudaraba: twelfth: mudaraba. (Miskin) Such as when he stipulates loss on the mudarib, the mudaraba is valid and the condition is void, and the loss is on the owner of capital. And if he stipulates ten dirhams from the profit, it becomes invalid (fasid) not from the aspect that it is invalidated by an invalid condition, for it is not invalidated by it, but rather due to cutting the partnership. (Fath) And judgeship: thirteenth: judgeship. As when the caliph appoints him to a certain town on condition that he is never dismissed, or appoints him permanently, the condition is void, and he may dismiss him even without offense. And governorship: fourteenth: governorship when the caliph says: (Ayni) I appoint you over it on condition that you do not ride. And in al-Bazzaziyya: if he stipulated on him that he not take bribes, or that he not drink wine, the appointment and the condition are valid. And if he does anything of that, he is dismissed. And judgeship and governorship are pure appointment and delegation, so it is permissible to add them (to time) and suspend them on a condition. (Zaylai, Fath) And suretyship: fifteenth: suretyship, and it is of the type of commitments (iltizamat), so it is permissible to add it to time and to suspend it on a suitable condition. And if the condition is unsuitable, the condition is corrupted and the suretyship is valid, such as when he says: I stand surety for your debtor on condition that you lend me such-and-such. And transfer of debt: sixteenth: transfer of debt when he says: I transfer you to so-and-so on condition that you do not revert upon him if he becomes insolvent. (Ayni) And it is among commitments which one does not take an oath on, so its suspension is not valid, except that it entails the debt upon him. (Ayni, Zaylai) And agency: seventeenth: agency (Ayni), and it is of the type of releases (itlaqat) and of the category of relinquishments (isqatat). So if he says: I appoint you as my agent to discharge me from what you have over me, he becomes an agent and the condition is void. And rescission: eighteenth: rescission (Miskin). Such as when a man buys a slave from another for one thousand dirhams and they take possession, then the seller says: Rescind (aqilni) so that I may defer the price for a year, and the buyer says: I rescind (aqaltu), the rescission is valid but not the deferral. (Zaylai, Fath) And kitaba: nineteenth: kitaba when he makes a kitaba contract on condition that he (the slave) does not leave Kufa without his permission, or that he does not deal with so-and-so, or that he work in a type of trade. The kitaba is valid with this condition and the condition is void; so he may leave the town and engage in whatever types of trade he wishes with any person he wishes. This is because this condition is not included in the core of the contract. But if it is included in the core of the contract such that it concerns the countervalue itself, like kitaba for wine and the like, then it is invalidated by it, because kitaba has resemblance to sale insofar as the slave is property in relation to the master, and resemblance to marriage insofar as it is not property in relation to himself. So we act on both resemblances: its resemblance to sale invalidates it if the corrupting element is in the core of the contract; and due to its resemblance to marriage, it is not invalidated by an extraneous condition. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 86/2] And permission to the slave etc.: twentieth: permission to the slave when he says to the people of the market: I have permitted this slave to trade on condition that he informs me; his permission is valid and the condition is void. And if he said to his slave: I permit you to trade for a month, ...
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage lists contracts that are not invalidated by an invalid condition (shart fasid). The key principle is that conditions are part of the prohibitions of riba, and apply only to financial exchanges (mu'awada maliyya). Non-financial exchange contracts remain valid even if an invalid condition is attached; the condition is simply void. The text provides examples for each contract: in a loan, if a condition benefits the lender, it is void (due to the hadith prohibiting loans that draw benefit); a gift with a condition of compensation is valid only if compensation is suitable money/goods, not mere abstention; charity, marriage, divorce, khul', emancipation, pawn, appointment, and will are all non-exchange contracts that remain valid. Further contracts like partnership, mudaraba, judgeship, governorship, suretyship, transfer of debt, agency, rescission, kitaba, and permission for a slave to trade are similarly unaffected by invalid conditions as long as the condition is not integral to the core (as in kitaba with wine). The commentary clarifies that for kitaba, if the condition is extrinsic, the contract is valid; if intrinsic (e.g., countervalue is wine), it is invalidated due to its resemblance to sale.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition that is not part of the contract's core requirements or permitted stipulations. According to the text, such conditions are void but do not invalidate non-exchange contracts.
معاوضة مالية (mu'awada maliyya): A financial exchange contract where property is transferred in return for countervalue, e.g., sale, lease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if someone marries a woman with the condition that she receive 100 dinars monthly as maintenance?
A) Both the marriage and the condition are valid.
B) The marriage is valid but the condition is void, and she gets maintenance of the like.
C) The marriage is invalid because the condition is invalid.
D) The condition is valid, but the marriage is void.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, invalid conditions only affect financial exchange contracts; in all other contracts, the condition is void and the contract stands.

Invalid Conditions in Contracts: The Hanafi Principle of Shart Fasid
Enumerating 27 items with rulings on invalid conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a fasid condition is void while the contract remains valid, and identify which conditions render a contract invalid when integral.

Core Idea
An invalid condition does not invalidate the contract unless it is integral to its core.

When parties attach a condition that contradicts Shari'ah, does the entire contract collapse? The Hanafi school distinguishes: most fasid conditions are void but leave the contract intact. This lesson unpacks twenty-seven applications of this rule across sales, partnerships, judiciary appointments, and more.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract or legal act
First, recognize the type of contract or act being discussed (e.g., sale, partnership, agency, etc.) and note its nature (commutative, non-commutative, release, delegation).
The passage covers 27 distinct items; each has its own ruling but follows the same principle.
2
Locate the condition and assess its validity
Identify the condition attached (e.g., 'on condition that you gift me', 'on condition that you not ride', etc.). Determine if the condition is inherently invalid (shart fasid) according to Shari'ah.
A condition is fasid if it contradicts the spirit of the contract or imposes an irrational restriction.
3
Determine if the condition is integral or external
Check whether the condition is part of the core of the contract (sulb al-'aqd) or a mere external stipulation. If it affects the essential equivalence or consideration, it is integral; otherwise, it is external.
For example, in kitabah, a condition restricting trade is external, while a condition for wine as consideration is integral.
4
Apply the ruling: contract valid, condition void
If the condition is external and fasid, the ruling is: the contract is valid (sahih) and the condition is void (batal). The contract stands without the condition.
This is the default for most items listed.
5
Note exceptions: when the condition is integral
If the condition is integral, the entire contract becomes fasid (invalid). Also, for pure delegations (tawliya) like judiciary, unsuitable conditions are void but the appointment remains; suitable conditions (e.g., no bribery) are valid and binding.
The passage notes these exceptions explicitly.

(عيني)] وهي من الالتزامات التي لا يحلف بها، فلا يصح تعليقه، إلا أنه يستلزم الدين عليه. (عيني، زيلعي) والوكالة: [ أي السابع عشر : الوكالة (عيني) وهي من باب الإطلاقات ومن جملة الإسقاطات، فلو قال: وكلتك على أن تبرئني مما لك علي، يصير وكيلاً ويبطل الشرط. والإقالة : [ أي الثامن عشر : الإقالة. (مسكين)] بأن اشترى رجل من آخر عبداً بألف درهم وتقابضا، ثم قال البائع أقلني حتى أؤخر لك الثمن سنة، فقال: أقلت، جازت الإقالة دون التأخير. (زيلعي، فتح) والكتابة [ أي التاسع عشرة: الكتابة بأن كاتب بشرط أن لا يخرج من الكوفة إلا بإذنه، أو على أن لا يعامل فلاناً، أو على أن يعمل في نوع من التجارة، فإن الكتابة على هذا الشرط تصح ويبطل الشرط، فله أن يخرج من البلد، ويعمل ما شاء من أنواع التجارة مع أي شخص شاء، وذلك لأن هذا الشرط غير داخل في صلب العقد، وأما إذا كان داخلاً في صلب العقد بأن كان في نفس البدل كالكتابة على خمر ونحوها، فإنها تفسد به؛ لأن للكتابة شبها بالبيع من حيث أن العبد مال في حق المولى، وشبها بالنكاح من حيث أنه ليس بمال في حق نفسه، فعملنا بالشبهين فشبهها بالبيع يفسد إذا كان المفسد في صلب العقد، ولشبهها بالنكاح لا تبطل بالشرط الزائد. [رمز الحقائق: ٨٦/٢] وإذن العبد إلخ [ أي العشرون: إذن العبد بأن قال لأهل السوق: أذنت لهذا العبد في التجارة بشرط أن يعلمني صح إذنه وبطل الشرط، ولو قال لعبده أذنت لك أن تتجر إلى شهر، يصح أو على أن تتجر في كذا، فإن إذنه يكون عاماً في التجارات والأوقات، ويبطل الشرط. [رمز الحقائق: ٨٦/٢] ودعوة الولد: أي الحادي والعشرون: دعوة الولد بأن قال للأمة التي ولدت منه: هذا الولد مني بشرط أن ترضى امرأتي. (عيني) والصلح عن دم العمد [ أي الثاني والعشرون ] الصلح بأن صالح ولي المقتول من القاتل عمداً على شيء بشرط الإقراض أو الإهداء فالصلح صحيح والشرط فاسد، ويسقط الدم؛ لأنه من الإسقاطات، فلا يحتمل الشرط والجراحة [ أي الثالث والعشرون ] الجراحة، أي وكذا يصح الصلح عن الجراحة التي فيها القصاص بأن صالح عن الموضحة على شيء بشرط الإقراض فيبطل الشرط ويصح الصلح ويسقط القصاص. (عيني، فتح) وعقد الذمة [ أي الرابع والعشرون ] عقد الذمة، بأن صالح الإمام على مال معلوم على أن يأخذه من الرؤوس أو من الأراضي خاصة لا يصح عقد الذمة. (عيني، مسكين) وتعليق الرد بالعيب [ أي الخامس والعشرون ] تعليق الرد... بأن قال: إن لم أرد هذا الثوب المعيب اليوم عليك رضیت فالشرط بالرد بسبب العيب باطل ويصح الرد. (عيني، فتح (معدن أو بخيار الشرط: [ أي السادس والعشرون: تعليق الرد بخيار الشرط بأن قال من له خيار الشرط رددت المبيع إن شاء فلان (عيني)] أي تعليق الرد بخيار الشرط بأن اشترى رجل شيئاً، وشرط الخيار لنفسه ثلاثة أيام، وقال: إن لم أرد المبيع اليوم فقد رضيت به، أو إن لم أفعل كذا فقد أبطلت خياري، فإنه يصح الرد ويبقى خيار الشرط، ويبطل شرط سقوطه. (عيني، فتح، معدن) وعزل القاضي: [ أي السابع والعشرون: عزل القاضي بأن قال الخليفة له عزلتك عن القضاء بشرط رضا فلان، فإنه ينعزل ويبطل الشرط؛ لأن هذه الأشياء كلها ليست بمعاوضة مالية فلا يؤثر فيها الشروط الفاسدة، وبقي مما لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد الصلح عن جناية الغصب والوديعة والعارية إذا ضمنها رجل وشرط فيها حوالة أو كفالة والحجر على المأذون وتسليم الشفعة والنسب.
Book of Sales, Chapter of Miscellaneous Topics: Partnership, Mudarabah, Judiciary, Governorship, Suretyship, Transfer of Debt, Agency, Rescission, Kitabah (contract of manumission), Permission for Slave to Trade. Partnership [the eleventh]: Partnership when one says 'I partnered with you on condition that you gift me such-and-such' etc., and they stipulate profit and loss equally, they said: the stipulation of loss is invalid, meaning it being half is invalid because it follows capital in disparity. Mudarabah [the twelfth]: Mudarabah when one stipulates loss on the mudarib, the mudarabah is valid and the condition is void, and the loss is upon the owner of capital; if he stipulates ten dirhams from the profit, it becomes invalid, not because it is invalidated by the invalid condition, but because it severs the partnership. (Fath) Judiciary [the thirteenth]: Judiciary, as when the caliph appoints him over a town on condition that he not be removed ever, or appoints him perpetually, the condition is void, and he has the right to remove him even without sin. Governorship [the fourteenth]: Governorship when the caliph says: I appoint you on condition that you not ride; and it is said in al-Bazzaziyyah: if he stipulates on him that he not take bribes or not drink wine, the appointment and condition are valid, and if he does any of that, he is removed. Judiciary and governorship are pure delegation, so it is permissible to add them to time and suspend them on condition. (Zayla'i, Fath) Suretyship [the fifteenth]: Suretyship is from the category of commitments, so it is permissible to add it to time and suspend it on a suitable condition; if the condition is unsuitable, the condition is void and the suretyship is valid, like when he says: I stand surety for your debtor on condition that you lend me such-and-such. Transfer of Debt [the sixteenth]: Transfer of debt when he says: I transfer you to so-and-so on condition that you not revert to me if he becomes insolvent. (Ayni) It is among commitments that are not sworn, so it is not valid to suspend it, except that it necessitates the debt upon him. (Ayni, Zayla'i) Agency [the seventeenth]: Agency (Ayni) is from the category of delegations and from the set of releases; so if he says: I appoint you agent to release me from what you have against me, he becomes an agent and the condition is void. Rescission [the eighteenth]: Rescission (Miskin) such as when a man buys a slave from another for one thousand dirhams and they receive from each other, then the seller says: rescind so that I may defer the price for a year, and he says: I rescind, the rescission is valid but the deferment is not. (Zayla'i, Fath) Kitabah [the nineteenth]: Kitabah when he contracts kitabah on condition that the slave not leave Kufa except with his permission, or that he not deal with so-and-so, or that he work in a certain type of trade, then the kitabah on this condition is valid and the condition is void; he may leave the city and do whatever trade he wishes with any person, because this condition is not integral to the contract. But if it is integral to the contract, i.e., in the consideration itself, like kitabah on wine or similar, then it is invalidated by it, because kitabah resembles sale in that the slave is property from the master's perspective, and resembles marriage in that he is not property regarding himself; we act on both resemblances: its resemblance to sale invalidates if the invalidating factor is integral to the contract, and its resemblance to marriage prevents invalidation by a superfluous condition. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 86/2] Permission for Slave [the twentieth]: Permission for a slave when he says to the market people: I have permitted this slave to trade on condition that he inform me, his permission is valid and the condition is void; if he says to his slave: I permit you to trade for a month, it is valid, or on condition that you trade in such-and-such, then his permission is general in trades and times, and the condition is void. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 86/2] Claim of Paternity [the twenty-first]: Claim of paternity when he says to the slave woman who gave birth to him: this child is from me on condition that my wife is pleased. (Ayni) Compromise for Intentional Homicide [the twenty-second]: Compromise when the guardian of the killed person makes a compromise with the intentional killer for something on condition of lending or gifting, the compromise is valid and the condition is void, and the blood is waived because it is from the category of releases, so it does not bear conditions. Wounds [the twenty-third]: Wounds, likewise the compromise for wounds that entail retaliation is valid; if he compromises for a head wound for something on condition of lending, the condition is void and the compromise is valid and retaliation is waived. (Ayni, Fath) Contract of Dhimmah [the twenty-fourth]: Contract of dhimmah when the imam makes a pact for a known wealth on condition that he take it from heads or from lands specifically, the contract of dhimmah is not valid. (Ayni, Miskin) Suspending the Right of Return due to Defect [the twenty-fifth]: Suspending the right of return due to defect when he says: If I do not return this defective garment to you today, I am pleased, then the condition of return due to defect is void and the return is valid. (Ayni, Fath (Ma'din) or Stipulated Option [the twenty-sixth]: Suspending return due to stipulated option when the one who has the stipulated option says: I have returned the sold item if so-and-so wills (Ayni), i.e., when a man buys something and stipulates an option for himself for three days and says: If I do not return the sold item today, I am pleased with it, or if I do not do such-and-such, I have voided my option, then the return is valid and the stipulated option remains, and the condition of its lapse is void. (Ayni, Fath, Ma'din) Removal of the Judge [the twenty-seventh]: Removal of the judge when the caliph says to him: I remove you from the judiciary on condition that so-and-so is pleased, then he is removed and the condition is void, because all these things are not financial commutative contracts, so invalid conditions do not affect them. And remaining from what is not invalidated by an invalid condition: compromise for the tort of usurpation, deposit, and loan if a man becomes guarantor for them and stipulates transfer of debt or suretyship, and interdiction on the authorized slave, and delivery of pre-emption, and paternity.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq (Book of Sales, Chapter of Miscellaneous Topics) enumerates twenty-seven specific contracts and legal acts, detailing the effect of attaching an invalid condition (shart fasid) to each. The overarching principle is that in most cases, the invalid condition is void (batal) while the contract or act remains valid (sahih); only when the condition is integral to the contract (dakhil fi sulb al-'aqd) does the entire contract become void. The passage follows a consistent pattern: for each item, it states the contract type, gives an example of a fasid condition, and then rules either that the contract is valid and the condition void, or that the contract is invalid. For instance, in partnership (shirkah), stipulating loss in equal shares is invalid because loss follows capital proportion; the condition is void but the partnership remains valid. In mudarabah, stipulating loss on the mudarib is void, and loss falls on the owner of capital. For judicial appointment (qada) and governorship (imarah), which are pure delegations (tawliya), the condition is void but the appointment stands; however, if the condition is suitable (like not taking bribes), it is valid and the appointee may be removed upon violation. Suretyship (kafalah) and transfer of debt (hawalah) are commitments (iltizamat); they can be added to time and suspended on suitable conditions; unsuitable conditions are void but the contract is valid. Agency (wakalah) is a delegation and a release (isqat); a condition to release the principal is void but agency is valid. Rescission (iqalah) is valid without the void condition. Kitabah (contract of manumission) is valid with external conditions; if the condition is integral (like kitabah for wine), the contract is void due to resemblance to sale. Permission for a slave to trade is generally valid; any condition restricting it is void. Claim of paternity (da'wat al-walad) is valid with void condition. Compromise for intentional homicide or wounds (sulh) is valid as it is a release, so conditions are void and the blood/retaliation is waived. Contract of dhimmah is invalid if the condition restricts the source of jizya. Suspending the right of return due to defect or stipulated option: the condition is void but the return or option remains. Removal of the judge (azl al-qadi) is valid with void condition. The passage concludes by listing additional acts not invalidated by fasid conditions: compromise for tort of usurpation, deposit, and loan when guaranteed with a condition of hawalah or kafalah, interdiction on the authorized slave, delivery of pre-emption, and paternity. This comprehensive enumeration serves as a memorization anchor for the Hanafi principle that fasid conditions in non-commutative acts (ghayr mu'awadat maliyyah) do not affect their validity.

Key Terms
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is invalid according to Shari'ah, but not entirely void; it does not affect the core contract unless it is integral to the contract.
الإسقاطات (al-isqatat): Releases or waivers, such as waiver of blood (dam) or right of return; these acts do not admit conditions because they are unilateral relinquishments.
صلب العقد (sulb al-'aqd): The core or essence of the contract; a condition that is integral to the contract ('ayn al-badal or essential term) can invalidate the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person makes a contract of mudarabah (silent partnership) and stipulates that any loss will be borne by the mudarib, what is the ruling?
A) The contract and condition are both valid.
B) The contract is valid but the condition is void; loss falls on the owner of capital.
C) The contract is void due to the invalid condition.
D) The contract is valid only if the mudarib agrees to bear the loss.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid condition does not invalidate the contract unless it is integral to the core of the contract; otherwise, only the condition is void.
