Classification of Contracts Regarding Invalid Conditions and Temporal Addition
Meta-classification of contractual acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given contract into one of six Hanafi categories regarding the effect of invalid conditions and permissibility of temporal addition, and state the ruling for each category.

Core Idea
Tamlikat (ownership transfers) cannot be suspended or future-dated; pure releases and leases allow it.

This passage provides a comprehensive classification of contracts based on how they interact with invalid conditions and temporal addition. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for determining the validity of contractual stipulations in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first three categories
Note the three categories from the earlier discussion: acts invalidated by fasid conditions, acts that cannot be suspended on a condition, and acts not invalidated by fasid conditions. List examples for each.
The examples include 27 items mentioned previously.
2
Recognize the additional three categories
The passage adds three more: acts that can be suspended (isqatat mahdah etc.), acts that can be added to future time (14 items), and acts that cannot be added to future time (10 items). Memorize the examples.
The reason for prohibition of tamlikat is the element of gambling (qimar).
3
Understand the rationale for tamlikat restriction
Tamlikat (sale, gift, marriage, etc.) cannot be conditional or future-dated because ownership must be immediate; delay introduces uncertainty akin to gambling.
Compare with pure releases (divorce) which can be conditional.
4
Apply the classification to new contracts
Given a contract not listed (e.g., salam, istisna), determine its category based on whether it is a tamlik or involves immediate transfer.
Salam is an exception – it is a sale but allowed due to specific texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الشيخ لله ذكر هنا ثلاثة أشياء: الأول: ما يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، والثاني: ما لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط، والثالث: ما لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة. وبقيت هنا ثلاثة أقسام أخرى: الأول: ما يجوز تعليقه بالشرط، وهو مختص بالإسقاطات المحضة التي يحلف بها كالطلاق والالتزامات التي يحلف بها كالحج ،والصلاة والتوليات كالقضاء والإمارة، والثاني: ما يجوز إضافته إلى المستقبل من الزمان وهو أربعة عشر : الإجارة وفسخها والمزارعة والمعاملة والمضاربة والوكالة، والكفالة والإيصاء، والوصية والقضاء والإمارة والطلاق والوقف والثالث ما لا يصح إضافته إلى الزمان، وهو عشرة: البيع وفسخه وإجازته، والقسمة والشركة، والهبة ،والنكاح والرجعة والصلح عن مال والإبراء عن الدين؛ لأن هذه الأشياء تمليكات، فلا يجوز إضافتها إلى الزمان كما لا يجوز تعليقها بالشرط؛ لما فيه من معنى القمار. (عيني، فتح)
Then know that the shaykh – may Allah have mercy on him – mentioned here three things: First: what is invalidated by invalid conditions. Second: what cannot be suspended on a condition. Third: what is not invalidated by invalid conditions. And there remain here three other categories: First: what is permissible to suspend on a condition, which is specific to pure releases that are sworn by, like divorce, and commitments that are sworn by, like Hajj and prayer, and delegations like judiciary and governorship. Second: what is permissible to add to future time, and it is fourteen: lease and its rescission, sharecropping (muzara'ah), sharecropping (mu'amalah?), mudarabah, agency, suretyship, bequest (isa'), will (wasiyyah), judiciary, governorship, divorce, and endowment (waqf). Third: what is not permissible to add to time, and it is ten: sale and its rescission and its permission, division (qismah), partnership (shirkah), gift, marriage, revocable return (ruj'ah), compromise for property (sulh 'an mal), and absolution from debt (ibra' 'an al-dayn); because these things are transfers of ownership (tamlikat), so it is not permissible to add them to time just as it is not permissible to suspend them on a condition, due to the element of gambling. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage from the same chapter provides a meta-classification by a shaykh (likely the commentator) of the various acts discussed. It divides them into six categories. The first three are derived from the previous enumeration: (1) acts that are invalidated by fasid conditions (i.e., where the condition causes the contract to become fasid, such as sale with an integral fasid condition, or kitabah on wine); (2) acts that cannot be suspended on a condition (taliq) at all; (3) acts that are not invalidated by fasid conditions (the majority of the 27 items – contracts like shirkah, mudarabah, etc., where the condition is void but the act remains valid). Then three additional categories expand the analysis: (4) acts that can be suspended on a condition, which are restricted to pure releases (isqatat mahdah) that are sworn upon (like divorce, as in 'if you enter the house, you are divorced'), and commitments that are sworn upon (like vowing to perform Hajj or prayer), and delegations like qada and imarah. (5) acts that can be added to future time (idafa ila al-mustaqbal), listing fourteen items: lease (ijarah) and its rescission, muzara'ah, mu'amalah (a type of sharecropping), mudarabah, agency, suretyship, bequest (isa'), will, judiciary, governorship, divorce, and waqf. (6) acts that cannot be added to future time, listing ten items: sale and its rescission and permission, division, partnership, gift, marriage, ruj'ah, compromise for property, and ibra' from debt. The reason given is that these are tamlikat (transfers of ownership), and adding them to future time or suspending on a condition would introduce an element of gambling (qimar). This classification is a useful tool for determining which contracts can conditionally be applied. The passage is from the commentary tradition (Ayni, Fath) and serves as a critical refinement of the matn.

Key Terms
الإسقاطات المحضة (al-isqatat al-mahdah): Pure releases or waivers that are unilateral and do not involve exchange; they can be suspended on conditions (like talaq).
الإضافة إلى الزمان (al-idafa ila al-zaman): Adding a contract to a future time (e.g., 'I sell you this house next month'); permissible only for certain acts like ijarah, not for tamlikat.
تمليكات (tamlikat): Transfer of ownership contracts; they cannot be suspended or added to future time because ownership must be immediate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, which of the following contracts CAN be added to future time (idafa ila al-zaman)?
A) Sale (bay')
B) Gift (hibah)
C) Lease (ijarah)
D) Marriage (nikah)

Key Takeaway
Tamlikat cannot be conditional or future-dated; only pure releases, leases, and certain delegations allow suspension or temporal addition.

Invalid Conditions Do Not Affect Non-Financial Acts
Rulings on invalid conditions and their effect on various legal acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that invalid conditions are void but the underlying act remains valid for non-financial legal acts, and apply it to examples such as isqatat and appointments.

Core Idea
Invalid conditions are void but the act remains valid for all non-financial exchanges.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi principle: an invalid condition attached to a legal act does not necessarily invalidate the act itself. The crucial factor is whether the act is a financial exchange (mu'awada maliyya) or not. Many acts like dropping rights, appointments, and settlements tolerate invalid conditions without being corrupted. Understanding this distinction prevents us from mistakenly voiding valid transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Nature of the Act
First, determine whether the legal act is a financial exchange (e.g., sale, marriage) or a non-financial act (e.g., dropping a right, appointment). This classification determines the effect of an invalid condition.
Non-financial acts include isqatat (dropping rights), appointments, and conditional returns.
2
Check for an Invalid Condition
Look for a condition that is legally invalid—such as a condition of lending or gifting in a settlement, or a condition on the pleasure of a third party in an acknowledgment.
Invalid conditions often involve uncertainty (gharar) or gambling (qimar) or are contrary to the nature of the act.
3
Apply the Hanafi Rule
If the act is NOT a financial exchange, the invalid condition is void but the act remains valid. If the act IS a financial exchange, the invalid condition may invalidate the entire act (e.g., sale with a void condition).
This rule is based on the principle that isqatat and appointments do not bear conditions, so the condition is simply ignored.
4
Confirm with Examples
Review the examples in the passage: acknowledgment of paternity with a condition of wife's pleasure (valid), settlement for intentional homicide with a condition of lending (valid, blood-feud drops), conditional return for defect (condition void, return valid), dismissal of judge with condition (dismissal valid).
Each example illustrates the rule that the act is not corrupted by the invalid condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الشرط ويصح .
أو على أن تتجر في كذا، فإن إذنه يكون عاماً في التجارات والأوقات، ويبطل الشرط. [رمز الحقائق: ٨٦/٢] ودعوة الولد: أي الحادي والعشرون: دعوة الولد بأن قال للأمة التي ولدت منه: هذا الولد مني بشرط أن ترضى امرأتي. (عيني) والصلح عن دم العمد [ أي الثاني والعشرون ] الصلح بأن صالح ولي المقتول من القاتل عمداً على شيء بشرط الإقراض أو الإهداء فالصلح صحيح والشرط فاسد، ويسقط الدم؛ لأنه من الإسقاطات، فلا يحتمل الشرط والجراحة [ أي الثالث والعشرون ] الجراحة، أي وكذا يصح الصلح عن الجراحة التي فيها القصاص بأن صالح عن الموضحة على شيء بشرط الإقراض فيبطل الشرط ويصح الصلح ويسقط القصاص. (عيني، فتح) وعقد الذمة [ أي الرابع والعشرون ] عقد الذمة، بأن صالح الإمام على مال معلوم على أن يأخذه من الرؤوس أو من الأراضي خاصة لا يصح عقد الذمة. (عيني، مسكين) وتعليق الرد بالعيب [ أي الخامس والعشرون ] تعليق الرد... بأن قال: إن لم أرد هذا الثوب المعيب اليوم عليك رضیت فالشرط بالرد بسبب العيب باطل ويصح الرد. (عيني، فتح (معدن أو بخيار الشرط: [ أي السادس والعشرون: تعليق الرد بخيار الشرط بأن قال من له خيار الشرط رددت المبيع إن شاء فلان (عيني)] أي تعليق الرد بخيار الشرط بأن اشترى رجل شيئاً، وشرط الخيار لنفسه ثلاثة أيام، وقال: إن لم أرد المبيع اليوم فقد رضيت به، أو إن لم أفعل كذا فقد أبطلت خياري، فإنه يصح الرد ويبقى خيار الشرط، ويبطل شرط سقوطه. (عيني، فتح، معدن) وعزل القاضي: [ أي السابع والعشرون: عزل القاضي بأن قال الخليفة له عزلتك عن القضاء بشرط رضا فلان، فإنه ينعزل ويبطل الشرط؛ لأن هذه الأشياء كلها ليست بمعاوضة مالية فلا يؤثر فيها الشروط الفاسدة، وبقي مما لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد الصلح عن جناية الغصب والوديعة والعارية إذا ضمنها رجل وشرط فيها حوالة أو كفالة والحجر على المأذون وتسليم الشفعة والنسب، ثم اعلم أن الشيخ لله ذكر هنا ثلاثة أشياء: الأول: ما يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، والثاني: ما لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط، والثالث: ما لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة. وبقيت هنا ثلاثة أقسام أخرى: الأول: ما يجوز تعليقه بالشرط، وهو مختص بالإسقاطات المحضة التي يحلف بها كالطلاق والالتزامات التي يحلف بها كالحج ،والصلاة والتوليات كالقضاء والإمارة، والثاني: ما يجوز إضافته إلى المستقبل من الزمان وهو أربعة عشر : الإجارة وفسخها والمزارعة والمعاملة والمضاربة والوكالة، والكفالة والإيصاء، والوصية والقضاء والإمارة والطلاق والوقف والثالث ما لا يصح إضافته إلى الزمان، وهو عشرة: البيع وفسخه وإجازته، والقسمة والشركة، والهبة ،والنكاح والرجعة والصلح عن مال والإبراء عن الدين؛ لأن هذه الأشياء تمليكات، فلا يجوز إضافتها إلى الزمان كما لا يجوز تعليقها بالشرط؛ لما فيه من معنى القمار. (عيني، فتح)
Chapter of Miscellaneous Matters. Book of Sales, and Acknowledgment of Paternity, and Settlement for Intentional Homicide and Wounds, and Contract of Dhimma, and Conditional Return for Defect or for Option of Condition, and Dismissal of Judge. The condition is invalid but the act is valid. Or that she trade in such and such, then his permission is general in trades and times, and the condition is void. [Sign of Truths: 86/2] And acknowledgment of paternity: i.e., the twenty-first: Acknowledgment of paternity by a man saying to his slave woman who gave birth from him: 'This child is from me on condition that my wife is pleased.' (Ayni) And settlement for intentional homicide: i.e., the twenty-second: Settlement by the heir of the slain with the intentional killer upon something with a condition of lending or gifting, then the settlement is valid and the condition is void, and the blood-feud is dropped because it is from acts of dropping (isqatat), so it does not bear conditions. And wounds: i.e., the twenty-third: Wounds, i.e., likewise the settlement for wounds that entail qisas is valid if he settles for a wound of the head (mudihah) upon something with a condition of lending, then the condition is void, the settlement is valid, and the qisas is dropped. (Ayni, Fath) And contract of dhimma: i.e., the twenty-fourth: Contract of dhimma, if the imam makes a settlement for a known wealth on condition that he takes it from heads or from lands specifically, the contract of dhimma is not valid. (Ayni, Miskin) And conditional return for defect: i.e., the twenty-fifth: Conditional return... such that he said: 'If I do not return this defective garment today to you, I am pleased' then the condition of return due to defect is void and the return is valid. (Ayni, Fath) Or with option of condition: i.e., the twenty-sixth: Conditional return with option of condition, such that the person who has the option of condition said: 'I return the sold item if so-and-so wishes' (Ayni). i.e., Conditional return with option of condition: that a man bought something and stipulated a three-day option for himself and said: 'If I do not return the sold item today, I am pleased with it,' or 'If I do not do such-and-such, I have annulled my option,' then the return is valid and the option of condition remains, and the condition of its fall is void. (Ayni, Fath, Ma'din) And dismissal of judge: i.e., the twenty-seventh: Dismissal of judge: that the caliph said to him: 'I dismiss you from the judiciary on condition of so-and-so's pleasure,' then he is dismissed and the condition is void; because all these things are not financial exchange, so invalid conditions do not affect them. And what remains of what is not invalidated by an invalid condition: settlement for the offense of usurpation, and trust (wadi'ah), and loan (ariyah) if a man guarantees them and stipulates therein a transfer (hawalah) or guarantee (kafalah), and interdiction of a permitted slave (hajr 'ala al-ma'dhun), and delivery of pre-emption (shuf'ah), and lineage (nasab). Then know that the master (shaykh) mentioned here three things: first, what is invalidated by invalid conditions; second, what is not valid to be conditioned; third, what is not invalidated by invalid conditions. And there remain three other categories: first, what is valid to be conditioned, which is specific to pure acts of dropping (isqatat) that one vows by, like divorce, and commitments that one vows by, like Hajj and prayer, and appointments like judiciary and emirate. Second, what is valid to be added to future time, and these are fourteen: Ijarah and its rescission, muzara'ah, mu'amalah, mudarabah, agency (wakalah), guarantee (kafalah), endowment (is'a'), bequest (wasiyyah), judiciary, emirate, divorce, and waqf. Third, what is not valid to be added to time, and these are ten: sale and its rescission and permission, division (qismah), partnership (shirkah), gift (hibah), marriage (nikah), return (ruj'ah), settlement for property, and discharge from debt (ibra'); because these are things of ownership (tamlikat), so it is not valid to add them to time just as it is not valid to condition them, due to the meaning of gambling (qimar) in that. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq is a compilation of rulings on the effect of invalid conditions in various legal acts that are not financial exchanges. The author lists several examples: acknowledgment of paternity with a condition of the wife's pleasure—the condition is void but the acknowledgment is valid; settlement for intentional homicide or wounds with a condition of lending—the settlement is valid and the blood or qisas is dropped because these are acts of dropping rights (isqatat) that do not tolerate conditions; contract of dhimma with a condition on specific sources of wealth—invalid; conditional return for defect or option—the condition is void but the return is valid; dismissal of a judge with a condition—dismissal is valid, condition void. The underlying principle is that invalid conditions do not affect acts that are not financial exchanges (mu'awada maliyya). The passage concludes with a classification: some acts are invalidated by invalid conditions, some cannot be conditioned at all, and some are not invalidated by invalid conditions. It also adds three more categories: acts that may be conditioned (pure isqatat and commitments), acts that may be added to future time (fourteen types including ijarah, agency, waqf), and acts that cannot be added to future time (ten types including sale, marriage, gift) because they are tamlikat (transfers of ownership) and deferral implies gambling.

Key Terms
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is legally invalid but added to a contract or legal act. In these rulings, it does not corrupt the act if the act is not a financial exchange.
الإسقاطات (al-isqatat): Legal acts that drop or waive rights, such as dropping blood-feud or qisas. These do not tolerate conditions; an invalid condition is void but the isqat remains valid.
التمليكات (al-tamlikat): Acts that transfer ownership, such as sale, gift, marriage. These cannot be added to future time or conditioned with invalid conditions because they would involve gambling (qimar).
المعاوضة المالية (al-mu'awada al-maliyya): A financial exchange contract, such as sale, where each party gives and receives something of value. Invalid conditions corrupt such contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT invalidated by an invalid condition?
A) Sale of a defective item with a condition on return
B) Settlement for intentional homicide with a condition of lending
C) Contract of dhimma with a condition on specific lands
D) Marriage with a condition that the wife has no right to maintenance

Key Takeaway
Invalid conditions are void but do not invalidate the underlying act when the act is not a financial exchange.

Classification of Acts: Conditioning, Deferral, and the Effect of Invalid Conditions
Classification of acts by effect of invalid conditions, conditioning, and deferral.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify legal acts into six categories based on their tolerance of invalid conditions, ability to be conditioned, and ability to be deferred, and apply the classification to new cases.

Core Idea
Acts are classified by whether they are invalidated by invalid conditions, can be conditioned, or can be deferred; financial exchanges are the most restricted.

The passage provides a comprehensive classification of legal acts in Hanafi fiqh into three categories (invalidated by invalid conditions, cannot be conditioned, not invalidated) and three additional categories (valid to condition, valid to defer, invalid to defer). Understanding this classification helps a jurist (faqih) quickly determine the effect of any condition or time element on a legal act. This lesson unpacks each category with examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Original Categories
The author first mentions three types: (1) acts invalidated by invalid conditions (financial exchanges), (2) acts that cannot be conditioned at all (pure isqatat and commitments), and (3) acts that are not invalidated by invalid conditions (isqatat and appointments). Note that categories 2 and 3 overlap but are distinguished by whether the act itself can be conditioned.
Category 2: cannot be conditioned, meaning even a valid condition is not allowed? The text says 'what is not valid to be conditioned' meaning you cannot attach any condition to it—the condition is automatically void. Category 3: even if an invalid condition is attached, the act remains valid.
2
Identify the Three Additional Categories
The author adds: (4) acts that may be conditioned (pure isqatat like divorce, commitments like Hajj, and appointments), (5) acts that may be added to future time (fourteen acts like ijarah, agency, waqf), and (6) acts that may not be added to future time (ten acts like sale, marriage, gift).
Category 4 overlaps with categories 2 and 3 but focuses on conditioning with a valid condition? Actually category 2 says cannot be conditioned, but here it says may be conditioned—this seems contradictory. The resolution: category 2 refers to invalid conditions? The text says 'ما لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط' meaning that attaching any condition (even valid?) is not valid for those acts. But category 4 says 'ما يجوز تعليقه بالشرط' meaning it is valid to attach a condition to these acts. So there are acts that cannot bear any condition (like divorce? But divorce is in category 4 as may be conditioned). This needs careful reading. Actually the classification is: (a) acts invalidated by invalid conditions, (b) acts whose conditioning is not valid (i.e., you cannot attach a condition even if it is valid? Because they are isqatat that don't bear conditions), (c) acts not invalidated by invalid conditions (meaning even if you attach an invalid condition, the act stands). Then additional: (d) acts that may be conditioned (these are pure isqatat that are done by oath, like divorce, and commitments like Hajj, and appointments). So (b) and (d) seem to conflict. Possibly (b) refers to acts where conditioning is not valid at all (like you cannot say 'I divorce you on condition that you give me money' because that would turn it into a financial exchange), while (d) refers to acts where conditioning is valid (like saying 'If I do X, then I divorce you' which is a valid conditional divorce). So we need to reconcile. For the guided path, we'll focus on the clear examples.
3
Apply the Classification to Examples
Given a specific act (e.g., sale, ijarah, divorce), determine which category it falls into and what the effect of an invalid condition or deferral would be.
Use the lists: e.g., sale is invalidated by invalid conditions and cannot be deferred; ijarah can be deferred; divorce cannot be invalidated by invalid conditions and can be conditioned and deferred.
4
Understand the Rationale
The rationale for why tamlikat (ownership transfers) cannot be conditioned or deferred is that they involve gambling (qimar) because future delivery creates uncertainty. Isqatat and appointments do not involve exchange, so conditions and deferral are permissible.
This rationale is explicitly mentioned in the passage: 'due to the meaning of gambling in that.'

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq is a compilation of rulings on the effect of invalid conditions in various legal acts that are not financial exchanges. The author lists several examples: acknowledgment of paternity with a condition of the wife's pleasure—the condition is void but the acknowledgment is valid; settlement for intentional homicide or wounds with a condition of lending—the settlement is valid and the blood or qisas is dropped because these are acts of dropping rights (isqatat) that do not tolerate conditions; contract of dhimma with a condition on specific sources of wealth—invalid; conditional return for defect or option—the condition is void but the return is valid; dismissal of a judge with a condition—dismissal is valid, condition void. The underlying principle is that invalid conditions do not affect acts that are not financial exchanges (mu'awada maliyya). The passage concludes with a classification: some acts are invalidated by invalid conditions, some cannot be conditioned at all, and some are not invalidated by invalid conditions. It also adds three more categories: acts that may be conditioned (pure isqatat and commitments), acts that may be added to future time (fourteen types including ijarah, agency, waqf), and acts that cannot be added to future time (ten types including sale, marriage, gift) because they are tamlikat (transfers of ownership) and deferral implies gambling.

Key Terms
التمليكات (al-tamlikat): Acts that transfer ownership, such as sale, gift, marriage. These cannot be added to future time or conditioned with invalid conditions because they would involve gambling (qimar).
الإسقاطات المحضة (al-isqatat al-mahdah): Pure acts of dropping rights, like divorce (dropping marriage tie) and dropping blood-feud. These may be conditioned or deferred in certain ways.
الإضافة إلى الزمان (al-idafah ila al-zaman): Adding a contract to a future time, i.e., deferring its effect. Some acts can be deferred (e.g., ijarah), others cannot (e.g., sale).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Sale
B) Gift
C) Ijarah
D) Marriage

Key Takeaway
Financial exchanges (tamlikat) are the most restricted: invalid conditions invalidate them, and they cannot be conditioned or deferred.

Sarf: Definition, Conditions, and the Ruling on Equality in Exchange
Definition of Sarf with conditions and hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-sarf according to the Hanafi school, state the two required conditions (tamathul and taqabud) for same-genus exchange, and explain the Hanafi ruling on addition or reduction before separation.

Core Idea
Sarf requires equality in weight and immediate hand‑to‑hand delivery; any excess invalidates the contract according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq opens the Book of Sarf (currency exchange). It defines the contract linguistically and legally, then lays out the essential conditions derived from a well‑known hadith. The text also records a key intra-Hanafi disagreement over what happens if one party adds or reduces the same genus before the exchange is complete. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate both the definition and the core conditions, and you will understand which opinion is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of Sarf
Read the opening sentences: 'هو بيع بعض الأثمان ببعض' and the commentary. Sarf is defined as the sale of some currencies (athman) for others – specifically gold and silver. Note the linguistic nuance: it is called Sarf because the two countervalues must be transferred hand to hand.
The text also mentions the four types of sales and places Sarf as the sale of debt for debt, making it the weakest category.
2
Extract the conditions for validity
The phrase 'فلو تجانسا شرط التماثل والتقابض' tells us that when the two currencies are of the same genus (e.g., gold for gold), two conditions are required: tamathul (equality in weight) and taqabud (hand‑to‑hand delivery). For different genera, only hand‑to‑hand is required.
Later the text adds that deferment (ajal) and option of condition (khiyar al‑shart) are also prohibited because they prevent immediate delivery.
3
Analyse the hadith proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith: 'الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة … مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء، يداً بيد' (Muslim). Identify the explicit commands: 'مثلاً بمثل' requires equality; 'يداً بيد' requires hand‑to‑hand. The phrase 'فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم' shows that when genera differ, equality is no longer required, but hand‑to‑hand remains.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al‑thubut) but its dalala is qati (clear meaning) for the Hanafi school.
4
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute on addition/reduction
The text says: if one party adds or reduces the same genus before separation, according to Imam Abu Hanifa the contract becomes invalid (fasid). Abu Yusuf says it remains valid. Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa on addition but permits reduction as an independent gift. Understand the thamarah al‑khilaf: under Abu Hanifa the contract must be rescinded; under Abu Yusuf it stands.
The relied upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa: addition invalidates. Reduction is treated as a separate gift, following Muhammad's view.
5
Confirm the mode of delivery: hand‑to‑hand, not vacating
The text explicitly states 'والتقابض باليد لا بالتخلية' – delivery must be by physical hand‑to‑hand transfer, not by vacating the premises (takhliyah). This applies to all forms of gold and silver: minted, unminted, and manufactured.
This is important because other schools may accept constructive delivery; Hanafis require actual physical transfer in the session.

أحكام الصرف
كتاب الصرف
في بيان أحكامه
هو بيع بعض الأثمان ببعض، فلو تجانسا شرط التماثل والتقابض،
أي الصرف شرعا
كتاب الصرف البيع بالنظر إلى المبيع أربعة أنواع: بيع العين بالعين، والعين بالدين، والدين بالعين، والدين بالدين، فلما بين الثلاثة الأول شرع في بيان الرابع، وإنما أخره؛ لأن بيع الدين بالدين وهو الصرف أضعف البياعات، حتى شرط قبض العوضين في المجلس وكان المناسب أن يعنوان بالباب؛ لكون الصرف من أنواع البيوع. والصرف لغة النقل والرد ، قال تعالى: ثُمَّ انْصَرَفُوا صَرَفَ اللهُ قُلُوبَهُمْ ﴾ (التوبة: ١٢٧) وسمي هذا البيع به؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى نقل بدليه من يد إلى يد، وله معنى آخر لغة وهو الفضل، ومنه سمي التطوع من العبادات صرفاً؛ لأنه زيادة على الفرائض، قال علي: "من انتمى إلى غير أبيه لا يقبل الله منه صرفاً ولا عدلاً" أي نفلاً ولا فرضاً، وسمي هذا البيع به؛ لأنه لا ينتفع بعينه، ولا يطلب منه إلا الزيادة. وركنه الإيجاب والقبول، أو التعاطي، وشرطه التقابض قبل الافتراق، ولهذا لم يصح فيه أجل ولا خيار شرط؛ لأن خيار الشرط يمنع ثبوت الملك أو تمامه، وذلك يخل بالقبض، فإن أسقطا الأجل والخيار في المجلس صح، ويدخله خيار العيب، ولا يتصور فيه خيار رؤية كسائر الديون؛ لأن خيار الرؤية ثابت في العين دون الدين، والمراد عن الدين النقد، ومن العين المصوغ من الأواني والحلي. (كفاية، فتح بعض الأثمان: أي ما خلق للثمنية، ومنه المصوغ. (ط) ببعض كالذهب والفضة إذا بيع أحدهما بالآخر أو بجنسه. (عيني) فلو تجانسا : أقسام الصرف ثلاثة: بيع الذهب بالذهب وبيع الفضة بالفضة، وبيع أحدهما بالآخر، ولابد فيه من قيود ثلاثة: أحدها: وجود التقابض من كل من الجانبين قبل التفرق بالأبدان والثاني: أن لا يكون فيه خيار، والثالث: أن لا يكون بدل الصرف مؤجلاً، فإن أبطل صاحب الخيار خياره قبل التفرق، أو أبطل صاحب الأجل أجله، ونقد ما عليه، ينقلب جائزاً، خلافاً لزفر فلو كان البدلان جنساً واحداً كالذهب بالذهب، والفضة بالفضة، شرط التساوي والتقابض معاً، ولو اختلف المتجانسان بأن كان أحدهما جيداً والآخر ردياً، أو اختلفا
من حيث الصياغة.
والأصل فيه قوله عليه: "الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة" إلى أن قال: "مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء، يداً بيد، فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم إذا كان يداً بيد"، رواه مسلم ،وآخرون، ونبه بشرط التماثل – أي التساوي في القدر وزناً - على أنه لو زاد أحدهما قبل الافتراق أو حط شيئاً من الجنس فسد عند الإمام، وقال أبو يوسف: لا يفسد، وهما باطلان ووافقه محمد في الزيادة، وجوز الحط كالهبة المستقلة، والعلم بتساويهما حالة العقد شرط صحته، والتقابض باليد لا بالتخلية، ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكونا مما يتعين بالتعيين كالمصوغ والتبر، أو لا يتعينان كالمضروب أو يتعين أحدهما دون الآخر؛ لإطلاق الحديث.
The Book of Sarf. 357. Rulings of Sarf. The Book of Sarf: regarding the explanation of its rulings. It is the sale of some currencies for others. If they are of the same type, equality and hand-to-hand delivery are required. That is, Sarf legally. The Book of Sarf: Sales according to the sold item are four types: sale of an 'ayn for an 'ayn, 'ayn for a dayn, dayn for ayn, and dayn for dayn. When he explained the first three, he began explaining the fourth, and delayed it because the sale of dayn for dayn, which is Sarf, is the weakest of sales, such that receipt of both countervalues in the session is required, and it was appropriate to title the chapter because Sarf is a type of sale. Linguistically, Sarf means transfer and return. Allah Most High said: {Then they turned away, Allah turned their hearts} (al-Tawbah 127). This sale is so named because it requires transferring its two substitutes from hand to hand. Another linguistic meaning is excess (fadl), and from that voluntary acts of worship are called Sarf because they are an increase over obligatory acts. Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'Whoever ascribes himself to other than his father, Allah will not accept from him Sarf nor 'Adl,' i.e., voluntary nor obligatory. This sale is so named because one does not benefit from its substance, but only seeks increase. Its pillar is offer and acceptance or mutual giving (ta'ati). Its condition is hand-to-hand delivery before separation. Therefore, deferment and option of condition are not valid in it because the option of condition prevents the establishment or completion of ownership, and that disrupts delivery. If they cancel the deferment and option in the session, it becomes valid. It admits option of defect, but option of sight is not conceivable in it like other debts because option of sight is established for 'ayn not for dayn. What is meant by dayn is cash ('ayn). (Kifayah, Fath) 'Some of the currencies': i.e., what is created for being a price (thumaniyyah), and includes manufactured items. (T) 'with some': like gold and silver when one is sold for the other or for its genus. (Ayni) 'If they are of the same type': Divisions of Sarf are three: sale of gold for gold, sale of silver for silver, and sale of one for the other. Three restrictions are necessary: first, hand-to-hand delivery from both sides before physical separation; second, that there is no option; third, that the substitute in Sarf is not deferred. If the holder of the option cancels his option before separation, or the holder of the deferment cancels the deferment and pays what is due, it becomes valid, contrary to Zufar. If the two countervalues are of the same genus, like gold for gold and silver for silver, equality and hand-to-hand are required together. If they differ in quality, one being good and the other bad, or they differ in minting. The basis for this is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Gold for gold, silver for silver,' up to his saying: 'like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand. If these types differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' Reported by Muslim and others. He indicated by the condition of equality (i.e., equality in weight) that if one party adds something before separation or reduces something of the same genus, it is invalid according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). Abu Yusuf said: It is not invalid; both opinions are invalid. Muhammad agreed with him (Abu Hanifa) regarding the addition, but allowed reduction as an independent gift. Knowledge of their equality at the time of contract is a condition of its validity. Hand-to-hand delivery is by hand, not by vacating (takhliyah). There is no difference in this between items that are specified by specification (like manufactured and raw gold) and those that are not specified (like minted coins), or one is specified and the other not, due to the generality of the hadith.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Sarf (currency exchange) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by defining Sarf as the sale of one currency for another, specifically gold and silver. The author places Sarf in the context of four types of sales: 'ayn for 'ayn, 'ayn for debt, debt for 'ayn, and debt for debt. Sarf is the fourth and weakest type because both countervalues are debts and must be exchanged hand-to-hand in the session. The term 'Sarf' is explained linguistically as transfer, return, and excess, with Quranic and hadith support. The pillar (rukn) of Sarf is offer and acceptance or mutual taking (ta'ati). The essential condition is hand-to-hand delivery before the parties separate; therefore, deferment and option of condition are invalid. However, option of defect is allowed, but option of sight is not because that applies only to physical goods ('ayn), not to debts (which are gold/silver). The passage then details three necessary restrictions: hand-to-hand delivery, no option, and no deferment. If the parties cancel these in the session, the contract becomes valid (contrary to Zufar). For transactions within the same genus (gold for gold, silver for silver), both equality in weight and hand-to-hand are required. The hadith from Muslim is cited as proof. The passage ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one party adds or subtracts some of the same genus before separation, Abu Hanifa rules the contract invalid; Abu Yusuf says it remains valid; Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa on addition but treats subtraction as an independent gift. Knowledge of equality at contract time is a condition, and delivery must be by hand, not by vacating the premises.

Key Terms
الصرف (al-sarf): The sale of one currency (gold or silver) for another, or the exchange of gold for gold or silver for silver. Legally, it is the sale of some prices (athman) for others.
التماثل (al-tamathul): Equality in weight (not quality) when the same genus is exchanged, e.g., gold for gold. Required for validity per hadith.
التقابض (al-taqabud): Mutual hand-to-hand delivery of both countervalues in the session before the parties separate. A condition of validity in Sarf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Sarf contract for the same genus (gold for gold), what two conditions are required according to the hadith cited in this passage?
A) Equality in weight and a fixed price
B) Equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery
C) Equality in number and written contract
D) Hand-to-hand delivery and a witness

Key Takeaway
Sarf requires two key conditions for same-genus exchange: equality in weight and immediate hand-to-hand delivery; any addition invalidates the contract per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Essential Conditions of Currency Exchange (Sarf)
Defines Sarf and its conditions with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Sarf, identify the two conditions (equality and hand-to-hand delivery) based on the hadith, and apply them to exchanges of same and different types of currency.

Core Idea
Sarf: same genus requires equality, different genus only hand-to-hand.

This lesson introduces Kitab al-Sarf, the chapter on currency exchange. The author defines Sarf, classifies sales, and establishes the conditions based on the prophetic hadith. Understanding these fundamentals is crucial before exploring the intra-madhhab differences in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and four types of sale
The text defines Sarf as sale of some commodities of value for others, and categorizes sales into four types. Note that Sarf is the sale of debt for debt, making it the weakest and requiring strict conditions.
Focus on the classification: 'ayn with 'ayn, 'ayn with dayn, dayn with 'ayn, dayn with dayn.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The author cites the well-known hadith about gold and silver. Identify the key phrases: 'like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand'.
The hadith is the primary dalil for the conditions.
3
Extract the two conditions
For same genus (gold for gold, silver for silver), both equality (tamathul) and hand-to-hand (taqabud) are required. For different genera (gold for silver), only hand-to-hand is required.
Equality is by weight, not count.
4
Note the additional restrictions
Sarf cannot involve deferment (ajal) or option (khiyar) because they impede possession. Option of defect is allowed, but option of sight is not.
These restrictions follow from the condition of hand-to-hand delivery.
5
Understand the condition for same genus with different quality
Even if the same genus differs in quality or workmanship, equality by weight is still required (since weight is textually established for currencies).
Workmanship does not change the ruling.

فقط دون التماثل
وإن اختلفا جودة وصياغة، وإلا شرط التقابض، فلو باع الذهب بالفضة مجازفَةً أي من حيث الجودة أي من حيث الصياغة صح إن تقابضا في المجلس، ولا يصح التصرف في ثمن الصرف قبل قبضه، فلو باع دينارا بدراهم واشترى بها ثوبا، فسد بيع الثوب، ولو باع أمة وهو عشرة دراهم ولم يقبض الدراهم بالدراهم في المجلس قبل قبض ثمن الصرف الفاء للنتيجة مع طوق، أي طوق فضة في عنقها ثم اختلفوا في القبض هل هو شرط صحة العقد أو شرط بقاء الصحة؟ فقيل : هو شرط الصحة، فعلى هذا ينبغي أن يكون القبض مقروناً بالعقد، إلا أن حالهما قبل الافتراق جعلت كحالة العقد تيسيراً، فإذا وجد القبض فيه يجعل كأنه وجد حالة العقد، فيصح، وقيل: هو شرط البقاء على الصحة، فلا يحتاج إلى هذا التقدير، والشرط أن يقبضا قبل الافتراق بالأبدان حتى لو ناما أو أغمي عليهما في المجلس، ثم تقابضا قبل الافتراق صح، جاز مع بخلاف خيار المخيرة، حيث يبطل بمجرد قيامها . وقوله : "وإن اختلفا جودة وصياغة" قيد إسقاط الصفة بالأثمان؛ لأنه لو باع إناء نحاس مثله، وأحدهما أثقل من الآخر، أن النحاس وغيره مما يوزن من الأموال الربوية أيضاً؛ لأن صفة الوزن في النقدين منصوص عليها، فلا يتغير النقود بالصنعة، ولا تخرج عن كونها موزوناً بتعارف جعلها عددياً لو تعورف ذلك، بخلاف غيرها؛ فإن الوزن فيه بالعرف، فيخرج عن كونه موزوناً بتعارف عدديته إذا صيغ وصنع. (عيني، فتح، عناية وغيره) وإلا: أي وإن لم يتجانسا بأن باع ذهبا بفضة. (عيني) مجازفة: أي بيعاً مجازفة أو بفضل. (ط، عيني) صح لأن المستحق هو القبض قبل الافتراق بالأبدان دون التسوية، فلا يضره الجزاف والفضل لما روينا. (عيني)] أي لو باع الذهب بالفضة جزافا يصح ولو كان مع الفضل؛ لاختلاف الجنس بشرط أن يتقابضا في المجلس، حتى لو مشيا إلى جهة واحدة أو ناما في المجلس أو أغمي عليهما، لا يبطل الصرف؛ لقول ابن عمر: "وإن وثب من سطح فتب معه، وقصته ما روي عن ابن جبلة، قال: سألت عبد الله بن عمر الله، فقلت: إنا نقدم أرض الشام ومعنا الورق الثقال النافقة وعندهم الورق الخفاف الكاسدة، فنبتاع ورقهم العشر بتسعة ونصف، فقال: "لا تفعل، ولكن بع ورقك بذهب واشتر ورقهم بالذهب، ولا تفارقهم حتى تستوفي، وإن وثب من سطح فئب معه" فعلم أن المستحق هو القبض قبل الافتراق، وإن افترقا في الصرف قبل قبضهما أو قبل قبض أحدهما بطل البيع؛ لفوات الشرط وهو القبض، ولو باع الذهب بالذهب مجازفة، ثم علما تساويهما قبل الافتراق صح، وبعده لا يصح؛ لفوات القبض المستحق بالعقد حقاً الله تعالى؛ إذ الربا ،حرام، خلافاً لزفر؛ فإنه يجوز عنده، وهو القياس؛ لأن الدراهم لا تتعين عيناً كانت أو ديناً. (عيني، عناية)
فسد بيع الثوب: لأنه إن كان جائزاً يفوت القبض، ويفسد بيع الثوب فقط، والصرف يكون على حاله، وعن زفر : أن هذا البيع يجوز؛ إذ النقود لا تتعين بالتعيين ديناً كانت أو عيناً، ألا ترى أنه لو أسلم ديناً عن المسلم إليه -
Book of Currency Exchange: In explaining its rulings. It is the sale of some commodities of value for others. If they are of the same type, equality and hand-to-hand delivery are conditions. i.e. Sarf in Islamic law. The book of Sarf: Sale is of four types by consideration of the sold item: sale of an item for an item, an item for a debt, a debt for an item, and a debt for a debt. When he explained the first three, he began explaining the fourth. He delayed it because the sale of debt for debt, which is Sarf, is the weakest of sales, to the extent that delivery of both countervalues was conditioned in the session. It was appropriate to title the chapter because Sarf is a type of sale. Sarf linguistically means transfer and rejection. Allah said: 'Then they turned away, Allah turned their hearts' (9:127). This sale is named so because it requires transferring the two countervalues from hand to hand. It has another linguistic meaning, surplus, hence voluntary acts of worship are called Sarf because they are additional to obligations. Ali (RA) said: 'Whoever claims lineage to other than his father, Allah does not accept from him Sarf nor Adl' i.e., optional nor obligatory. This sale is named so because its essence is not benefited from, and nothing but surplus is sought from it. Its pillar is offer and acceptance, or mutual giving. Its condition is hand-to-hand delivery before separation. Therefore, a deferred payment and option condition are not valid in it because option prevents the establishment or completion of ownership, and that impairs delivery. If they cancel the deferment and option in the session, it becomes valid. Option of defect enters it, but option of sight is not conceivable in it like other debts, because option of sight is established in a specific item, not in a debt. What is meant by debt is cash, and by specific item is manufactured vessels and jewelry. (Kifayah, Fath: Some commodities of value: i.e., what is created for being a price, including manufactured items. (T) with some like gold and silver when one is sold for the other or for its own type. (Ayni) So if they are of the same type: The divisions of Sarf are three: sale of gold for gold, sale of silver for silver, and sale of one for the other. Three restrictions are necessary: one: existence of hand-to-hand delivery from both sides before bodily separation; second: no option; third: the price in Sarf is not deferred. If the option holder cancels his option before separation, or the deferment holder cancels his deferment and pays what he owes, it becomes valid, contrary to Zufar. If the two countervalues are of the same type, like gold for gold and silver for silver, equality and hand-to-hand delivery are both conditions. If the two of the same type differ in quality, one being good and the other bad, or differ in workmanship. The basis for it is his (PBUH) statement: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver' until he said: 'like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand. If these categories differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' Reported by Muslim and others. He indicated by the condition of equality i.e., equality in quantity by weight, that if one of them gives extra before separation or reduces something from the same type, it becomes invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: it does not become invalid, both are invalid. Muhammad agreed with him regarding the extra but permitted the reduction like an independent gift. Knowledge of their equality at the time of the contract is a condition for its validity. Hand-to-hand delivery is by hand, not by clearing (takhliyah). There is no difference in this between items that are specific by identification like manufactured items and bullion, or not specific like coins, or one specific and not the other, due to the generality of the hadith. Only without equality. And if they differ in quality and workmanship, otherwise the condition is hand-to-hand. So if one sells gold for silver roughly i.e., in terms of quality i.e., workmanship, it is valid if they take possession in the session. Disposal of the price in Sarf before receiving it is not valid. So if one sells a dinar for dirhams and buys a cloth with them, the sale of the cloth is invalid. If one sells a female slave and it is ten dirhams and he did not receive the dirhams for the dirhams in the session before receiving the price of Sarf, so the result, with a necklace i.e., a silver necklace around her neck. Then they differed about possession: is it a condition for the validity of the contract or a condition for the continuation of validity? It is said: it is a condition for validity. On this, possession should be concurrent with the contract, except that their state before separation is made like the state of the contract for facilitation. So if possession occurs within it, it is as if it occurred at the time of the contract, so it is valid. And it is said: it is a condition for the continuation of validity, so it does not need this estimation. The condition is that they take possession before bodily separation, to the extent that if they slept or fainted in the session, then took possession before separation, it is valid. It is permissible contrary to the option of the Mukhayyara (when a woman is given choice in divorce) which becomes void simply by her standing. His statement: 'And if they differ in quality and workmanship' is a restriction for dropping the attribute in currencies; because if he sold a copper vessel similar to it, one heavier than the other, copper and other weighable ribawi goods also, because the attribute of weight in the two monetary metals is textually established, so currency is not changed by workmanship, and does not cease to be weighable by convention of counting if that is conventional, contrary to other things; weight in them is by custom, so it ceases to be weighable by convention of counting when manufactured and worked. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah, etc.) Otherwise: i.e., if they are not of the same type, meaning he sold gold for silver. (Ayni) Roughly: i.e., a rough sale or with excess. (T, Ayni) It is valid because what is required is hand-to-hand possession before bodily separation, not equality, so rough and excess do not harm due to what we have narrated. (Ayni) i.e., if he sold gold for silver roughly, it is valid even if there is excess, due to difference of type, with the condition that they take possession in the session. So even if they walk to one direction or sleep in the session or faint, Sarf is not invalidated; due to the saying of Ibn Umar: 'Even if he jumps from a roof, follow him.' The story is as narrated from Ibn Jabalah who said: I asked Abdullah ibn Umar (RA), saying: We go to the land of Sham and we have heavy, well-circulating dirhams, while they have light, non-circulating dirhams. So we buy their ten dirhams for nine and a half. He said: 'Do not do that, but sell your dirhams for gold, and buy their dirhams with gold, and do not leave them until you receive. Even if he jumps from a roof, go with him.' So it is known that what is required is possession before separation. If they separate in Sarf before both receive or before one receives, the sale is invalid due to loss of the condition, which is possession. If one sells gold for gold roughly, then they know they are equal before separation, it is valid; after separation it is not, due to loss of the required possession by the contract as a right of Allah; for riba is forbidden, contrary to Zufar, for it is valid according to him, and it is the analogy because dirhams do not become specific whether as a specific item or debt. (Ayni, Inayah) The sale of the cloth becomes invalid: because if it was valid, possession would be lost, and only the sale of the cloth becomes invalid, while the Sarf remains as it was. From Zufar: that this sale is valid because currency does not become specific by identification whether debt or specific item, do you not see that if one gives a debt as capital in salam to the one who owes him -
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of Sarf (currency exchange) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by defining Sarf as the sale of some commodities of value (thaman) for others, specifically gold and silver. It classifies sales into four types and notes that Sarf is the sale of debt for debt, which is the weakest type, hence requiring strict conditions: hand-to-hand delivery (taqabud) in the session before separation. The author discusses linguistic origins and the hadith 'Gold for gold, silver for silver...' as evidence. The key conditions are equality (tamathul) when the same genus, and hand-to-hand delivery (taqabud) when different genera. Intra-Hanafi disputes are mentioned: regarding excess reduction (hittah) and increase (ziyadah) in the same genus, Abu Hanifa invalidates both, Abu Yusuf invalidates neither, while Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf on increase but allows reduction. The passage also covers delivery by hand vs. clearing, the impermissibility of deferred payment or option, and the effect of possession on contract validity. It cites the story of Ibn Umar advising not to exchange dirhams with excess but to go through gold, emphasizing hand-to-hand delivery. Finally, it addresses the invalidity of buying cloth with dirhams from Sarf before receiving them, and Zufar's contrary view.

Key Terms
صرف (Sarf): Sale of some commodities of value (thaman) for others, specifically gold, silver, and currency; the weakest type of sale requiring hand-to-hand delivery and equality when same genus.
مثلاً بمثل (mithlan bi-mithl): Equality in quantity by weight; required when exchanging same genus (gold for gold, silver for silver) to avoid riba.
تقابض (taqabud): Hand-to-hand delivery of both countervalues in the session before separation; a condition for validity of Sarf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if you sell 1 gold coin for 10 silver coins and you both take possession immediately, the contract is:
A) Invalid because equality is not met.
B) Valid because they are different genera.
C) Invalid because hand-to-hand is missing.
D) Valid only if the weight of silver equals gold.

Key Takeaway
Sarf requires immediate hand-to-hand delivery; equality is only needed when the same type of currency is exchanged.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Rulings on Excess, Reduction, and Possession in Sarf (Intra-Hanafi Disputes)
Intra-Hanafi disputes on excess, reduction, and possession conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the different Hanafi positions on excess and reduction in same-genus Sarf, and apply the rule that possession must occur before separation.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa invalidates both excess and reduction; the mufta bihi view is strict equality.

This lesson builds on the conditions of Sarf by examining the intra-madhhab disagreements over what happens when an excess or reduction occurs in same-genus exchange. It also explores the nature of possession, including cases of sleeping or fainting, and the ruling on disposing of the purchased currency before receipt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute on excess and reduction
The text states that if one party increases or decreases the amount of the same genus, Abu Hanifa invalidates the contract, Abu Yusuf validates it, and Muhammad allows reduction but not excess.
Note the three distinct positions.
2
Analyze the proof for each position
The hadith requires equality; Abu Hanifa sees any imbalance as riba. Abu Yusuf considers reduction as an independent gift. Muhammad distinguishes between the two.
The hadith is the common proof; interpretation differs.
3
Understand the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, that both excess and reduction invalidate the contract.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
4
Examine the condition of possession (qabd)
The text discusses whether possession is a condition for the validity of the contract or for its continuation. The preferred view is that it is a condition for continuation, so if they sleep and then take possession before separating, it is valid.
This nuance affects cases of temporary separation.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
The text gives examples: selling gold for silver roughly (valid), selling gold for gold roughly (invalid unless they know equality before separation), and the Ibn Umar story.
Note the importance of timing of knowledge.

كتاب الصرف
في بيان أحكامه
هو بيع بعض الأثمان ببعض، فلو تجانسا شرط التماثل والتقابض،
أي الصرف شرعا
كتاب الصرف البيع بالنظر إلى المبيع أربعة أنواع: بيع العين بالعين، والعين بالدين، والدين بالعين، والدين بالدين، فلما بين الثلاثة الأول شرع في بيان الرابع، وإنما أخره؛ لأن بيع الدين بالدين وهو الصرف أضعف البياعات، حتى شرط قبض العوضين في المجلس وكان المناسب أن يعنون بالباب؛ لكون الصرف من أنواع البيوع. والصرف لغة النقل والرد ، قال تعالى: ثُمَّ انْصَرَفُوا صَرَفَ اللهُ قُلُوبَهُمْ ﴾ (التوبة: ١٢٧) وسمي هذا البيع به؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى نقل بدليه من يد إلى يد، وله معنى آخر لغة وهو الفضل، ومنه سمي التطوع من العبادات صرفاً؛ لأنه زيادة على الفرائض، قال علي: "من انتمى إلى غير أبيه لا يقبل الله منه صرفاً ولا عدلاً" أي نفلاً ولا فرضاً، وسمي هذا البيع به؛ لأنه لا ينتفع بعينه، ولا يطلب منه إلا الزيادة. وركنه الإيجاب والقبول، أو التعاطي، وشرطه التقابض قبل الافتراق، ولهذا لم يصح فيه أجل ولا خيار شرط؛ لأن خيار الشرط يمنع ثبوت الملك أو تمامه، وذلك يخل بالقبض، فإن أسقطا الأجل والخيار في المجلس صح، ويدخله خيار العيب، ولا يتصور فيه خيار رؤية كسائر الديون؛ لأن خيار الرؤية ثابت في العين دون الدين، والمراد عن الدين النقد، ومن العين المصوغ من الأواني والحلي. (كفاية، فتح بعض الأثمان: أي ما خلق للثمنية، ومنه المصوغ. (ط) ببعض كالذهب والفضة إذا بيع أحدهما بالآخر أو بجنسه. (عيني) فلو تجانسا : أقسام الصرف ثلاثة: بيع الذهب بالذهب وبيع الفضة بالفضة، وبيع أحدهما بالآخر، ولابد فيه من قيود ثلاثة: أحدها: وجود التقابض من كل من الجانبين قبل التفرق بالأبدان والثاني: أن لا يكون فيه خيار، والثالث: أن لا يكون بدل الصرف مؤجلاً، فإن أبطل صاحب الخيار خياره قبل التفرق، أو أبطل صاحب الأجل أجله، ونقد ما عليه، ينقلب جائزاً، خلافاً لزفر فلو كان البدلان جنساً واحداً كالذهب بالذهب، والفضة بالفضة، شرط التساوي والتقابض معاً، ولو اختلف المتجانسان بأن كان أحدهما جيداً والآخر ردياً، أو اختلفا من حيث الصياغة.
والأصل فيه قوله عليه: "الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة" إلى أن قال: "مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء، يداً بيد، فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم إذا كان يداً بيد"، رواه مسلم ،وآخرون، ونبه بشرط التماثل – أي التساوي في القدر وزناً - على أنه لو زاد أحدهما قبل الافتراق أو حط شيئاً من الجنس فسد عند الإمام، وقال أبو يوسف: لا يفسد، وهما باطلان ووافقه محمد في الزيادة، وجوز الحط كالهبة المستقلة، والعلم بتساويهما حالة العقد شرط صحته، والتقابض باليد لا بالتخلية، ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكونا مما يتعين بالتعيين كالمصوغ والتبر، أو لا يتعينان كالمضروب أو يتعين أحدهما دون الآخر؛ لإطلاق الحديث.
فقط دون التماثل
وإن اختلفا جودة وصياغة، وإلا شرط التقابض، فلو باع الذهب بالفضة مجازفَةً أي من حيث الجودة أي من حيث الصياغة صح إن تقابضا في المجلس، ولا يصح التصرف في ثمن الصرف قبل قبضه، فلو باع دينارا بدراهم واشترى بها ثوبا، فسد بيع الثوب، ولو باع أمة وهو عشرة دراهم ولم يقبض الدراهم بالدراهم في المجلس قبل قبض ثمن الصرف الفاء للنتيجة مع طوق، أي طوق فضة في عنقها ثم اختلفوا في القبض هل هو شرط صحة العقد أو شرط بقاء الصحة؟ فقيل : هو شرط الصحة، فعلى هذا ينبغي أن يكون القبض مقروناً بالعقد، إلا أن حالهما قبل الافتراق جعلت كحالة العقد تيسيراً، فإذا وجد القبض فيه يجعل كأنه وجد حالة العقد، فيصح، وقيل: هو شرط البقاء على الصحة، فلا يحتاج إلى هذا التقدير، والشرط أن يقبضا قبل الافتراق بالأبدان حتى لو ناما أو أغمي عليهما في المجلس، ثم تقابضا قبل الافتراق صح، جاز مع بخلاف خيار المخيرة، حيث يبطل بمجرد قيامها . وقوله : "وإن اختلفا جودة وصياغة" قيد إسقاط الصفة بالأثمان؛ لأنه لو باع إناء نحاس مثله، وأحدهما أثقل من الآخر، أن النحاس وغيره مما يوزن من الأموال الربوية أيضاً؛ لأن صفة الوزن في النقدين منصوص عليها، فلا يتغير النقود بالصنعة، ولا تخرج عن كونها موزوناً بتعارف جعلها عددياً لو تعورف ذلك، بخلاف غيرها؛ فإن الوزن فيه بالعرف، فيخرج عن كونه موزوناً بتعارف عدديته إذا صيغ وصنع. (عيني، فتح، عناية وغيره) وإلا: أي وإن لم يتجانسا بأن باع ذهبا بفضة. (عيني) مجازفة: أي بيعاً مجازفة أو بفضل. (ط، عيني) صح لأن المستحق هو القبض قبل الافتراق بالأبدان دون التسوية، فلا يضره الجزاف والفضل لما روينا. (عيني)] أي لو باع الذهب بالفضة جزافا يصح ولو كان مع الفضل؛ لاختلاف الجنس بشرط أن يتقابضا في المجلس، حتى لو مشيا إلى جهة واحدة أو ناما في المجلس أو أغمي عليهما، لا يبطل الصرف؛ لقول ابن عمر: "وإن وثب من سطح فتب معه، وقصته ما روي عن ابن جبلة، قال: سألت عبد الله بن عمر الله، فقلت: إنا نقدم أرض الشام ومعنا الورق الثقال النافقة وعندهم الورق الخفاف الكاسدة، فنبتاع ورقهم العشر بتسعة ونصف، فقال: "لا تفعل، ولكن بع ورقك بذهب واشتر ورقهم بالذهب، ولا تفارقهم حتى تستوفي، وإن وثب من سطح فئب معه" فعلم أن المستحق هو القبض قبل الافتراق، وإن افترقا في الصرف قبل قبضهما أو قبل قبض أحدهما بطل البيع؛ لفوات الشرط وهو القبض، ولو باع الذهب بالذهب مجازفة، ثم علما تساويهما قبل الافتراق صح، وبعده لا يصح؛ لفوات القبض المستحق بالعقد حقاً الله تعالى؛ إذ الربا ،حرام، خلافاً لزفر؛ فإنه يجوز عنده، وهو القياس؛ لأن الدراهم لا تتعين عيناً كانت أو ديناً. (عيني، عناية)
فسد بيع الثوب: لأنه إن كان جائزاً يفوت القبض، ويفسد بيع الثوب فقط، والصرف يكون على حاله، وعن زفر : أن هذا البيع يجوز؛ إذ النقود لا تتعين بالتعيين ديناً كانت أو عيناً، ألا ترى أنه لو أسلم ديناً عن المسلم إليه -
Book of Currency Exchange: In explaining its rulings. It is the sale of some commodities of value for others. If they are of the same type, equality and hand-to-hand delivery are conditions. i.e. Sarf in Islamic law. The book of Sarf: Sale is of four types by consideration of the sold item: sale of an item for an item, an item for a debt, a debt for an item, and a debt for a debt. When he explained the first three, he began explaining the fourth. He delayed it because the sale of debt for debt, which is Sarf, is the weakest of sales, to the extent that delivery of both countervalues was conditioned in the session. It was appropriate to title the chapter because Sarf is a type of sale. Sarf linguistically means transfer and rejection. Allah said: 'Then they turned away, Allah turned their hearts' (9:127). This sale is named so because it requires transferring the two countervalues from hand to hand. It has another linguistic meaning, surplus, hence voluntary acts of worship are called Sarf because they are additional to obligations. Ali (RA) said: 'Whoever claims lineage to other than his father, Allah does not accept from him Sarf nor Adl' i.e., optional nor obligatory. This sale is named so because its essence is not benefited from, and nothing but surplus is sought from it. Its pillar is offer and acceptance, or mutual giving. Its condition is hand-to-hand delivery before separation. Therefore, a deferred payment and option condition are not valid in it because option prevents the establishment or completion of ownership, and that impairs delivery. If they cancel the deferment and option in the session, it becomes valid. Option of defect enters it, but option of sight is not conceivable in it like other debts, because option of sight is established in a specific item, not in a debt. What is meant by debt is cash, and by specific item is manufactured vessels and jewelry. (Kifayah, Fath: Some commodities of value: i.e., what is created for being a price, including manufactured items. (T) with some like gold and silver when one is sold for the other or for its own type. (Ayni) So if they are of the same type: The divisions of Sarf are three: sale of gold for gold, sale of silver for silver, and sale of one for the other. Three restrictions are necessary: one: existence of hand-to-hand delivery from both sides before bodily separation; second: no option; third: the price in Sarf is not deferred. If the option holder cancels his option before separation, or the deferment holder cancels his deferment and pays what he owes, it becomes valid, contrary to Zufar. If the two countervalues are of the same type, like gold for gold and silver for silver, equality and hand-to-hand delivery are both conditions. If the two of the same type differ in quality, one being good and the other bad, or differ in workmanship. The basis for it is his (PBUH) statement: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver' until he said: 'like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand. If these categories differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' Reported by Muslim and others. He indicated by the condition of equality i.e., equality in quantity by weight, that if one of them gives extra before separation or reduces something from the same type, it becomes invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: it does not become invalid, both are invalid. Muhammad agreed with him regarding the extra but permitted the reduction like an independent gift. Knowledge of their equality at the time of the contract is a condition for its validity. Hand-to-hand delivery is by hand, not by clearing (takhliyah). There is no difference in this between items that are specific by identification like manufactured items and bullion, or not specific like coins, or one specific and not the other, due to the generality of the hadith. Only without equality. And if they differ in quality and workmanship, otherwise the condition is hand-to-hand. So if one sells gold for silver roughly i.e., in terms of quality i.e., workmanship, it is valid if they take possession in the session. Disposal of the price in Sarf before receiving it is not valid. So if one sells a dinar for dirhams and buys a cloth with them, the sale of the cloth is invalid. If one sells a female slave and it is ten dirhams and he did not receive the dirhams for the dirhams in the session before receiving the price of Sarf, so the result, with a necklace i.e., a silver necklace around her neck. Then they differed about possession: is it a condition for the validity of the contract or a condition for the continuation of validity? It is said: it is a condition for validity. On this, possession should be concurrent with the contract, except that their state before separation is made like the state of the contract for facilitation. So if possession occurs within it, it is as if it occurred at the time of the contract, so it is valid. And it is said: it is a condition for the continuation of validity, so it does not need this estimation. The condition is that they take possession before bodily separation, to the extent that if they slept or fainted in the session, then took possession before separation, it is valid. It is permissible contrary to the option of the Mukhayyara (when a woman is given choice in divorce) which becomes void simply by her standing. His statement: 'And if they differ in quality and workmanship' is a restriction for dropping the attribute in currencies; because if he sold a copper vessel similar to it, one heavier than the other, copper and other weighable ribawi goods also, because the attribute of weight in the two monetary metals is textually established, so currency is not changed by workmanship, and does not cease to be weighable by convention of counting if that is conventional, contrary to other things; weight in them is by custom, so it ceases to be weighable by convention of counting when manufactured and worked. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah, etc.) Otherwise: i.e., if they are not of the same type, meaning he sold gold for silver. (Ayni) Roughly: i.e., a rough sale or with excess. (T, Ayni) It is valid because what is required is hand-to-hand possession before bodily separation, not equality, so rough and excess do not harm due to what we have narrated. (Ayni) i.e., if he sold gold for silver roughly, it is valid even if there is excess, due to difference of type, with the condition that they take possession in the session. So even if they walk to one direction or sleep in the session or faint, Sarf is not invalidated; due to the saying of Ibn Umar: 'Even if he jumps from a roof, follow him.' The story is as narrated from Ibn Jabalah who said: I asked Abdullah ibn Umar (RA), saying: We go to the land of Sham and we have heavy, well-circulating dirhams, while they have light, non-circulating dirhams. So we buy their ten dirhams for nine and a half. He said: 'Do not do that, but sell your dirhams for gold, and buy their dirhams with gold, and do not leave them until you receive. Even if he jumps from a roof, go with him.' So it is known that what is required is possession before separation. If they separate in Sarf before both receive or before one receives, the sale is invalid due to loss of the condition, which is possession. If one sells gold for gold roughly, then they know they are equal before separation, it is valid; after separation it is not, due to loss of the required possession by the contract as a right of Allah; for riba is forbidden, contrary to Zufar, for it is valid according to him, and it is the analogy because dirhams do not become specific whether as a specific item or debt. (Ayni, Inayah) The sale of the cloth becomes invalid: because if it was valid, possession would be lost, and only the sale of the cloth becomes invalid, while the Sarf remains as it was. From Zufar: that this sale is valid because currency does not become specific by identification whether debt or specific item, do you not see that if one gives a debt as capital in salam to the one who owes him -
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of Sarf (currency exchange) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by defining Sarf as the sale of some commodities of value (thaman) for others, specifically gold and silver. It classifies sales into four types and notes that Sarf is the sale of debt for debt, which is the weakest type, hence requiring strict conditions: hand-to-hand delivery (taqabud) in the session before separation. The author discusses linguistic origins and the hadith 'Gold for gold, silver for silver...' as evidence. The key conditions are equality (tamathul) when the same genus, and hand-to-hand delivery (taqabud) when different genera. Intra-Hanafi disputes are mentioned: regarding excess reduction (hittah) and increase (ziyadah) in the same genus, Abu Hanifa invalidates both, Abu Yusuf invalidates neither, while Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf on increase but allows reduction. The passage also covers delivery by hand vs. clearing, the impermissibility of deferred payment or option, and the effect of possession on contract validity. It cites the story of Ibn Umar advising not to exchange dirhams with excess but to go through gold, emphasizing hand-to-hand delivery. Finally, it addresses the invalidity of buying cloth with dirhams from Sarf before receiving them, and Zufar's contrary view.

Key Terms
صرف (Sarf): Sale of some commodities of value (thaman) for others, specifically gold, silver, and currency; the weakest type of sale requiring hand-to-hand delivery and equality when same genus.
مثلاً بمثل (mithlan bi-mithl): Equality in quantity by weight; required when exchanging same genus (gold for gold, silver for silver) to avoid riba.
تقابض (taqabud): Hand-to-hand delivery of both countervalues in the session before separation; a condition for validity of Sarf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid because reduction is permissible.
B) Valid if they both agree.
C) Invalid due to reduction.
D) Invalid only if the reduction was not intended as a gift.

Key Takeaway
In same-genus Sarf, any deviation from equality invalidates the contract per the mufta bihi view; possession must occur before separation.

The Nature of Qabd in Sarf: Condition for Validity or Continuation?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the role of qabd in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi opinions on whether possession in sarf is a condition for validity or continuation, and state the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
In sarf, possession is a condition—but its timing determines whether the contract is initially valid or only continues valid.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the legal nature of possession (qabd) in currency exchange (sarf). The two opinions hinge on whether qabd is a condition for the initial validity of the contract (shart al-sihhah) or a condition for the continuation of its validity (shart al-baqa'). The difference leads to distinct legal consequences, especially regarding the permissibility of delays such as sleeping or fainting in the session. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the Hanafi condition theory in mu'amalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Opinions
Read the first sentence: 'Then they differed regarding possession: is it a condition for the validity of the contract or a condition for the continuation of validity?' Note the two positions exactly.
The opinions are presented without naming proponents – this is an intra-Hanafi difference.
2
Analyze the First Opinion (Shart al-Sihhah)
The first view requires possession to be concurrent with the contract. However, to facilitate practice, the period before separation is treated as an extension of the contract time. So if possession occurs in that period, it is retroactively considered to have occurred at contract formation.
This involves a legal fiction (taqdir) – treating the session as part of the contract moment.
3
Analyze the Second Opinion (Shart al-Baqa')
The second view holds that possession is a condition for the contract's continued validity. The contract is valid initially even without immediate possession, but if the parties separate without possessing, it becomes invalid. The text emphasizes that no legal fiction is needed.
Under this view, sleeping or fainting in the session does not nullify the contract as long as possession occurs before physical separation.
4
Understand the Exception (Khiyar al-Mukhayyara)
The passage notes an exception: the option of the woman given choice in marriage (khiyar al-mukhayyara) becomes void merely by her standing up from the session. This contrasts with the leniency in sarf.
This exception highlights that the leniency is specific to the nature of currency exchange.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text does not explicitly state the relied-upon view, but later Hanafi scholarship prefers the second opinion (shart al-baqa') because it avoids legal fiction and is more practical.
The mufta bihi is the second view: qabd is a condition for continuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلفوا في القبض هل هو شرط صحة العقد أو شرط بقاء الصحة؟ فقيل : هو شرط الصحة، فعلى هذا ينبغي أن يكون القبض مقروناً بالعقد، إلا أن حالهما قبل الافتراق جعلت كحالة العقد تيسيراً، فإذا وجد القبض فيه يجعل كأنه وجد حالة العقد، فيصح، وقيل: هو شرط البقاء على الصحة، فلا يحتاج إلى هذا التقدير، والشرط أن يقبضا قبل الافتراق بالأبدان حتى لو ناما أو أغمي عليهما في المجلس، ثم تقابضا قبل الافتراق صح، جاز مع بخلاف خيار المخيرة، حيث يبطل بمجرد قيامها.
Then they differed regarding possession: is it a condition for the validity of the contract or a condition for the continuation of validity? It was said: It is a condition for validity, accordingly possession should be concurrent with the contract, except that their state before separation is treated like the state of the contract for facilitation, so if possession occurs in it, it is considered as if it occurred at the time of the contract, so it is valid. And it was said: It is a condition for the continuation of validity, so this estimation is not needed, and the condition is that they take possession before separation by bodies, even if they sleep or become unconscious in the session, then take possession before separation, it is valid. It is permissible with the exception of the option of the woman given choice (mukhayyara), where it becomes void merely by her standing up.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal nature of possession (qabd) in currency exchange (sarf). Two opinions are recorded. The first view holds that possession is a condition for the validity (sihhah) of the contract itself, meaning the contract is not valid unless possession occurs. However, to facilitate practical transactions, the period before the parties separate from the session is considered like the time of the contract; so if they take possession before separation, it is retroactively valid. The second view holds that possession is a condition for the continuation (baqa') of validity, meaning the contract is initially valid but becomes invalid if they separate without possession. According to this view, the contract remains valid even if they sleep or become unconscious in the session, as long as they take possession before physically separating. The text notes an exception: the option of the woman given choice in marriage (khiyar al-mukhayyara) becomes void simply by her standing up from the session, unlike the leniency here. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the second view, as it avoids the need for retroactive estimation and is more practical. This dispute is a classical usul al-fiqh issue: whether a condition is part of the cause or part of the requirement for continuation.

Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Physical taking possession of the exchanged items in the session.
شرط الصحة (shart al-sihhah): A condition for the legal validity of the contract; without it the contract is void ab initio.
شرط البقاء على الصحة (shart al-baqa' 'ala al-sihhah): A condition for the continued validity of the contract; the contract is initially valid but becomes invalid if the condition is not fulfilled before separation.
التقدير (al-taqdir): Legal estimation or fiction; treating the session as an extension of the contract moment.
خيار المخيرة (khiyar al-mukhayyara): The option given to a woman in marriage to choose her husband, which expires if she stands up from the session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the status of a currency exchange contract if the parties sleep in the session and then take possession before separating?
A) The contract is void because possession must occur at the moment of contract.
B) The contract is valid because possession is a condition for continuation.
C) The contract is void because sleeping invalidates the session.
D) The contract is valid only if they had an agreement to tolerate sleep.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sarf, the relied-upon opinion is that possession (qabd) is a condition for the continuation of the contract's validity, not its initial formation, allowing for practical flexibility.
